Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 The first method is to make three or four cauteries, aligned according to the length of the urine, following the shape of the liver cautery that we mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient lie on their back; another method of cauterization is to heat the cautery which has two edges, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and raise the area where the urine is located, or let the ribs of the patient come towards the left side, and let the elevation with which you raise the area be according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After, he places the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced from the other side, and then pull out through the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see this, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the treatment when he has had pus for a long time, and this is different from the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	 of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Cautery is not useful for those with dropsy, except in the manner called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned in the divisions, and your treatment does not benefit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the navel, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cautery be very close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	 After leave the cautery open to drain pus for a long time, and do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	 The form of the cautery for the belly should be the shape that we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	 Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in those who are dropsical and are full of yellow bile, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply; thus, it would burn beyond the desired area. Let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	 After that, make two cauterizations on each leg at the point of the knee joint; and let the cauterization be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauterizations to heal for a long time without curing, so that the pus exits; afterwards, cure the other cauterizations as we have said.
de la menoison	 of the humors
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	 When the swelling of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of treatment; and you see the patient is strong and of great virtue, then make one large cauterization on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, making a circular cauterization; and four subtle cauterizations around the navel, each cauterization being a subtle nail head, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	 And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, perform cautery on the armpit, and one cautery on each eye, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	 of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and caused by cold and moist corrupted humors, and if they are treated as we have said by division and it does not help, then perform three cauteries: on the spine of the back, those that are entirely under the buttocks, a little at a time in a triangular shape; and one cautery between the buttocks two fingers wide; and if you think his stomach is cold, and the food is not cooked, and you see the face swell, then make one large cautery on the stomach as described above, and another on the liver, and another on the bladder with all the cauteries open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	 of the fleshiness which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	 When you cut into the fleshiness called "thelul", heat up the cautery that resembles a razor and then place it fully lit on the cut fleshiness; and leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of fleshiness, cauterize each one as we have said; after curing with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchatim, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	 of an improperly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	 When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such a disease occurs that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 When a fistula comes to someone, and it is inflamed and emits foul-smelling pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe it with a very fine tent, and ensure that you know the depth of the entire tent.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 After heating the cautery that looks like a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the depth at which the tent has entered, and continue with the cautery until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned once, or twice, or three times, depending on how much is needed; and beware of burning the nerves in it, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the fistula goes to the bladder and intestines, beware of these places, and do not perform this procedure except in a fleshy place, and know that it is not permanent; after caring for the place until it heals, and if the place is healed and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the place is pierced, and the bone is corrupted at the bottom; and thus as one of those that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	 Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	 When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from excessive windiness, and there is no desire for a woman, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on the kidneys, one part and another, with the cautery clavicle that we have previously mentioned; and if we perform cautery in the middle, there will be III cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater help.
de la vessie	 of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	 When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the lower part of the bladder, where the hairs of the pubis begin, and one cautery on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the knuckle of a thumb; and if you need to make two cauteries on the back, do so; and let the cautery be made according to the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	 against the retention
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	 When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the menstrual flow is corrupted and delayed in its onset; and when it comes, there is great pain: then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the back; and let the cautery be clavicle-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	 Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	 When the viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and if the site of dislocation is found, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and let the cautery be such that it has been used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if this cautery is not present, then make three large olive-sized cauteries, and let the cautery be as deep as all the hearts; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	 of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	 When pain comes to the hip joint due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of excessive humors with fetid pills or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 After that, you perform cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with burning medicine, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Fire cautery is according to many methods, one of which is this: you make three triangular cauteries on the hip joint, deep and wide, with a space between each the width of a finger, and the cautery should be olive-shaped. Sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four like this:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if you see it, then cauterize it with the circle cautery that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip; but do so in such a way that the circle contains the entire hip, and all the circumference of the circle is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the manner in which one proceeds with sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are made where the patient says the pain is located; and one cautery above the ankle at four fingers' width on the left side, slightly; and let the cautery be done with a razor blade, and let the circumference of the circle be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near there, then cauterize where he feels the pain three times or four with the cautery which is called "point."  /> And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are made where the patient says the pain is located; and one cautery above the ankle at four fingers' width on the left side, slightly; and let the cautery be done with a razor blade, and let the circumference of the circle be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or near there, then cauterize where he feels the pain three times or four with the cautery which is called "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	 Et si est besoing, que li en face plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genolz vers la cuisse, que li fai cautere au cautere cutellier ou circulier, et te donne bien garde en tes cauteres que tu n’i laissies mie tant le cautere que tu bruses les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraccion.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the entire leg was swollen, as well as the foot, and all the foot was pierced and corrupt.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a treatment for a stomach ailment from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, which is thus the manner, make one such iron and let it be at the head as thick as a thimble of a finger, or a little less, and let it be between-toothed, and let there be from one tooth to another the space of a walnut; and let the teeth be on two sides, and let them also be like noses, and let there be one handle of well-made iron; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then put it on the hip of the sick person, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery, and leave it for three days; and then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, continue the care until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	 Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its look, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured, and there where it is necessary.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of medicine that is burning thus you should make the instrument with intertwining threads on which the margin of the door descends, and it should be of brass or iron with one long wall, and in its height there are two nooses, and between each there is the thickness of a finger; and they are open from below and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Then place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and then place your hand very high on the box of the hip; then throw between the two circles of the awl hot iron that is heated in the fire a little, and leave it there for an hour of time, and let the patient endure the heat and the burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it experiences burning, as from fire; and when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with gentle warmth, and leave it thus for three days, and put on butter so that the black of the burn is removed; and let it be for three days until the corruption is drawn out; and this would be the last aid after the treatment of onions until it heals.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that dyes with heat according to what you have done on the hip in the same way; and this is the manner of hot heat, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicines.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and live coal, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 And let there be a small hole in it so that the tip of a razor can enter; and put another well-lead potted vessel over that pot, and put quicklime and coal and sweet water on top, until there are two fingers' width of liquid above the powders, then you will have taken it well in hand; and leave it thus until it descends as clear water into the leaded pot, then take all that water and throw it onto the coal and onto the quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very clear and ready for many works of medicine and for other members' cauteries; because it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip well, such as terebinth and honey anacardium and coal mixed together with soap.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was healed of the pain in the hip and the sciatic vein, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other cure was done, and that he was cured with one treatment when this cure was done, and he bathed as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says that you should take green and fresh and dry litargire, and grind it very well with a little fat, and apply it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and let it sit; and leave it for three hours, and in such quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed, and put him to bed, and all the pain will go away and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 Et sachez que nul ne doit user de cautère de telles médecines, si ce n'est après l'évacuation du corps.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with wool of goat, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe of the foot and the other one called phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards take dry goat wool and burn it to charcoal, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is smoldering; and do this again, and do not cease doing so until you think by sense that it reaches up to the hip, and that the pain stops; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat".
de la dolor dou dos	 of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	 When pain comes to the back, either from falling or striking or too great an evacuation, or from the appearance of cold matter spreading, in none of these cases is it worthwhile to use cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary that after the patient has been emptied of fetid pills or other similar things, one should make on the back, where the pain lies, three lines with signet ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "poin"; and if you wish, make IIII cauteries in the middle of the cautery clavile following this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	 Many times this disease comes to small children, and the sign of its beginning is that they have a narrow furrow when they rise, and fear; and you find in the back of the neck and in us the appearance that comes over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	 When you see this and you wish to cure it, then you cauterize it with the cautery of celce according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the cautery penetrates each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three lines long, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to a swollen place that is in pain from nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	 Of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	 When the pain of the joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which doctors call "podagra" properly, and when it is from cold causes and cannot be cured by medicines, it is cured by cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary that you prick on the surface of the foot, make a cautery at the point called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain comes up to the knees and other joints, which often happens, make three or four cauteries on each knee from each part, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand longer than until the tip of the iron is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 Et si les douleurs descendent jusqu'au genou et au dos, administrez-lui la cautérisation que nous avons mentionnée dans ce chapitre.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 Et si les douleurs sont dans les mains, faites deux lignes de points autour du poignet; et s'il reste encore des douleurs dans les doigts, faites alors des points sur chaque articulation et sur le dos de la main; et si les douleurs montent jusqu'aux épaules ou jusqu'aux côtes, cautérisez chaque partie, et assurez-vous de bien soigner le patient et de lui faire prendre des médicaments.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 Et car si vous prenez bien soin de lui et que vous purgez la fièvre, il sera guéri avec l'aide de Dieu.
de la routure dou syfac	 Of the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When rupture occurs in the shoulders, and the shoulders descend to the hips, recently, then it is necessary that when you see him treated, that he does not eat that day; and he uses things that let out wind, so that the feces come out of his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm until the shoulders are repaired, and bring them to your fingers, and place under the rupture on the wrist bone, and all one sign that should be similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which is this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then reset the joints to their place; and let the servant hold his hands above so they do not return back; and properly work the thighs on the patient, and place a pillow and a cloth on the thighs, and another on the foot that holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign until your hand is full, and the right one and the left one until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you reach the bone; and subtly watch that the joint does not protrude when making the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and thus the patient will not die or have other ills.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And the cautery of children should be fine according to their measure, and for large people also large according to their measure; after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; then cure with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it should be long before he gets up to walk in rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let a well-made belt be brought to him, and let him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, that he exert himself little and guard against excessive drinking and eating, and against too much shouting; and when he follows this teaching, then he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	 of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, make the fire cautery again according to its size, and burn one third of the circumference; after the treatment as we have said; and some of the ancients said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged fire according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the place and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below it, and then hold your hand in the middle of the entire cauterization tool.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and more delicate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	 of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 if it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, repeat another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it must move to the limb nearest to it, therefore you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	 of blending
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The messengers are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see it cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not diminish or disappear, and you doubt that the corruption might spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head toward the crown, and the other towards the forehead at the hairline; and two on each temple, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and enough so that the scales come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the neck as described before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	 And if the mischief is spread everywhere; and it clearly diminishes, then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned earlier, one cautery on the top of the nose, two on the spine of the neck, six on the spine of the back, one large on the buttock and another nearby, two on each shoulder, two on each ribcage, two on the tendons of the foot, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the heel, so you do not burn them; sometimes one cauterizes on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do of cautery, the more help I give, and it brings him profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cautery as the healthy ones do, because his body is already entirely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and the joints, as you will find them in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After treatment, dust the place with flour of vetch mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling comes in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the member according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little into the thickness of the skin; then cure it with onions until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes one cauterizes both the hand and the foot and the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb; and thus the swelling is removed; nevertheless, let no one interfere with this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	 from scars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the disease called "albaras" awakens, and medicinal ingredients are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of pea flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and colocynth blood and almond blood, each in equal parts; mix everything together, bind it with a cloth, and leave it in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	 The cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When cancer first appears and you see it spreading, then cauterize it with the cautery that resembles a circle, all around the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 Nevertheless, the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; nevertheless, this does not seem good to me because I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen sometimes; and it is more appropriate that it be cauterized around it with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	 Of the inflammation that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in healing either because of the excessiveness it causes or due to the patient's age when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of time; and you see that it is hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards, leave it thus.  ("adubelati" is likely a misspelling of "abubilatum", an old name for a chronic ulcer or sore.)
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you see her pierce with all the cautery, then heat the cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it outside in such a way that the course of the corruption is made clear.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the treatment until he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	 the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 There is another manner of disease which is called "corrodens," and is nothing other than a gnawing away of the limbs, for it gnaws at the limbs just as fire does with dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries both very small and large, according to what is needed for the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around until you have extracted all the corruption, so that nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupt may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and put on the places that have been cauterized a poultice with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of tumors producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, that is good; and if it does not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupt place.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this disease has sometimes been cured with cold medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the cure of cold medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	 of leeks that grow at the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often it happens that at the feet, on the outside, a disease grows which is called "clots" according to our intention, and it is a large hairy thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Cautery with fire is done by heating a cauterizing tool like the quill of a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron so that it can cover the nail on all sides, and there should be subtle edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to emit pus; then make a plaster of crushed wild mallows with vinegar, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the burn site by applying ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned outside the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, you must apply a cautery of hot water. It is done like this: take an iron or brass tube, or a goose quill, and place it on the wart and the corn, that is to say, for small warts; and put the tube on so that it covers all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the tube comes to the root of the wart, and the hot water can penetrate deeply to the root. And let the patient endure the stinging of the hot water for an hour; then leave them like this, and it will be completely uprooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 So do one after another, until you remove all those that are on the body, then treat the swellings that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	 treat the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 When some shake from coldness of the nerves, or from tertian fever or another cause, you must make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach at the umbilical point; this will stop the shaking, and speed up the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	 stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes appear on the surface of the body washed with water, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 If it is necessary at the beginning when they appear, make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery from myrtle wood, whose tip is taken to the fire, or a long root of Aristolochia, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the superfluities that cause them are destroyed, and they are healed; but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	 When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 Often there is a great outpouring of blood from the artery that is cut in the wound that comes afterwards, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very serious matter to stop it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 And yet when this happens to someone, hasten to place your finger on the wound of the vein, and press hard until the blood is stilled under your finger, and no drop comes out; then put in the fire several small and large olive-shaped cauteries until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is found, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood is coagulated.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	 And if it spurts when you remove your finger from the vein and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 Et ne cessez pas de faire cela l'un après l'autre tant que le sang soit arrêté; et veillez à ne pas brûler le nerf qui se trouve à côté, et qu'aucune autre mauvaise chose n'arrive au patient; et sachez que lorsque le sang coule de l'artère, on ne peut pas bien l'arrêter, surtout si l'artère est grande, sauf par une des quatre manières que nous avons dites: par cautérisation, ou par extraction si elle n'est pas traitée, ou par un fort lien de fil, ou par des médicaments appliqués qui ont le pouvoir d'arrêter le sang; et qu'il soit lié et maintenu fermement.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	 Whoever manages this will use a tight bandage of cloth or place burning objects on it, or similar things, if it is not beneficial or possible otherwise.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 And if this happens to someone and he does not have a doctor or medicine at hand, then he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind it well until it is closed over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the thumb, but often moisten it with very cold water so that the blood is frozen and swollen and closed; and make the inquiries for what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	 Here begins the second book on the treatment of hernias
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 Nous vous avons dit dans le premier chapitre toutes les maladies pour lesquelles il est nécessaire de faire un cautère avec du feu, ou des médicaments brûlants, et les questions et les causes et les instruments et les formes des cautères; et j’ai mis ce chapitre des cheveux de la tête jusqu'aux pieds, et je vais dans ce chapitre suivre le même chemin pour que vous trouviez plus facilement ce que vous cherchez.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	 And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one concerning cautery, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many types of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 if they come from such people who are so affected by their illness that they die easily because of the madness it brings and the severity of its harm; these are to be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are those who give you their word and say, "wait, I am healed"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this manner, but put greater concern on your honor than on your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of, and from which you can gain praise; and use prognosis and diagnosis in the treatment of your patients so that they may be healed. This will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and praiseworthy memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	 Very dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	 Now I have arranged this chapter for you by chapters, according to what is in the previous chapter on cautery, which I have discussed with you from head to toe, so that you can find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	 head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife presses too hard on the child's head; sometimes it happens for reasons unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen death has come quickly; and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work of such cures alone.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger each day until it could not support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone on the spine, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you split open the head with a wide incision; and it should be as long as II our fingers, so that the moisture drains out; and behold here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	 If the moisture is greater, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 Et si le moisture est sous l'os, et les signes que tu vois sont les commissures du chef ouvertes de chaque côté, et il y a un saut brusque lorsque tu presses de ta main à l'intérieur, et cela ne te répond pas: alors il faut que tu fasses trois fentes dans le chef selon cette manière:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Afterwards, bind the fentes with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then remove the bindings, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and allow the head to set evenly, and give the patient dry food of little moisture until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	 And another method of incision is that you observe where the maturity of the abscess appears, and the gathering of pus; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 Cut there where the abscess appears, and the gathering of pus, and make the incision according to your ability; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and let there be a flow of blood, so that the patient does not die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	 of inflammation
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	 When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or nose, and the illness is longstanding, and medical treatment does not help, then the final cure is to use cautery, with which two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 It is therefore necessary that when you see the blood vessels, the patient should move back his head; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the veins appear, then the patient should pull his neck taut with the cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the place of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are not far apart; then mark the places well, then cut each with a sharp spatula of two parts, until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be as wide as the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	 And if you see, push the spatula under the vein and cut above it, cutting also as two halves across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	 And when the vein is cut, the blood constantly spurts out.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery is not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the space of three fingers, then strike and dig down to the bone; and this amount of blood to let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone a point of bone spur, cut it so that such abscesses do not come, then bind the wound and bandage it, and the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	 of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	 When an ancient headache comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old foolishness and similar things, and he is treated by various methods of medicine and all this does not benefit him at all, then we will extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls back the hair of his temples, and looks for the artery that appears in the temple, because it appears well through its pulsation, and it is little hidden except in some men who are too cold; and if it is hidden, then let the patient stretch his neck with some strips, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and wash the area with hot water until the artery clearly appears; then take the spatula whose form is this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up with tweezers, and separate it well from the tissues that are underneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, then twist it around the tip of a hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, then the blood will not come out at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 And draw blood for six times up to three; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and let the bleeding come out gradually; then cut off the excess that is between the two knots in that same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with the knife cautery down to the bone until the fingers are cut off; and this is a mutilating work, if the patient has fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 Because the cautery is used to finish with moisture: for this reason, it is of greater use against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 And when extracting the arteries, one must fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made compresses; and when they are removed, let them be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and with compresses, until they heal; and if there is bleeding from the artery as long as you work there, then hasten to the copper pot for cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the blood is coagulated; and if you do not have this present, then press the place with your finger until the blood is congealed, and wash the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold it as needed; and this which is lighter and easier to extract from the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting in two parts, but let the cuts be well spaced to preserve their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	 Car when the instrument is too blunt, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And there must be one inch between the two knives, and when you have stitched together the two places, and you place the burning iron upon it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let them be far apart because it is not completely healed from this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	 tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on top of the temple of the forehead, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the patient's face turning red, and they feel a sensation in their forehead as if shaking; and their eyes are dim and wet so that the hair of the eyelids has fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
