Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure for contusion," and this is what you should do for a patient with this illness: make sure he has hairs on his forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; one of the incisions should be like two fingers deep into the forehead from top to bottom until the neck, and the other two on both temples above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on the temples above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbone, and each wound should be three fingers wide across the joint; have ready a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp spatula on both sides as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 From the incision that is in front of the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two cuts as far as the skin above the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract strongly this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 Place in the first cut the instrument called “scraper,” which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And put the sharp side towards the flesh of the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it opens the heart, and then make another cut in the middle incision to the other outside; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the taken blood; then put in each cut a tent of old cotton, and put on damp cloths with wine and oil and vinegar, and see that pustules do not come there; and on the third day release the bandage, and bring a great amount of hot water, then the cure of ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 of the humor of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When someone has an acute cataract commonly, and you see the eyes dim and small, and weakening the vision, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and there is a severe headache, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that those substances and this cataract come from many veins, and the cure for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from the left eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton wool and linen cloths between the two lips of the incision, then bind with dampened cloths in wine and oil on top, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then cure with drying substances, which make the flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice with them; and administer it in these wounds to draw out all the flesh.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 About ear obstruction
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains or beetles, stones such as iron, or seeds such as peas, beans, and lentils; or fluid substances such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear that does not belong there and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, then drop a little bit of violet oil or sesame oil into it, and administer an extractive treatment; and make them sneeze with spices, and plug their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear upwards. ︎
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Many times a fever comes from this treatment; and if the fever does not come, he should administer an extraction with subtle pincers, for which is the form here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If the fever comes from the pincers, it is good; if not, then administer an extraction with a subtle onion, of small double-pored variety; and if it does not come from that, make a cane of bronze and insert the tip of the cane into the ear hole firmly, and stop up what is around the cane with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the cane; then draw out the fever strongly, for many times a fever comes as we have said; and if the fever does not come in this manner, take glue from which birds take, and put it into some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw out the fever.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess or spasm comes there; and the way of the cutting is such that you first make a sign on the patient with cephalic, and extract blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it hangs; and let the cut be like a moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly to your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer an extracting medicine; and if it cannot come out, then administer a subtle laxative according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision for that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear; then make many incisions for it until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tweezers and in the sieve, as we have said, so that the extraction may be thorough.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In the case of water falling into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first use sneezing condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If she jumps through the roof, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 if the roof is not there, then take many small stones according to the length of your thumb, light and thin, and heat them slightly in the fire; and have the patient insert one into the opening of her ear, and jump on her feet on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus she jumps out completely; and if you see, then take a reed, and insert one end into the ear, and hold the other end in the fire until the longest part of the reed is burnt; then repeat the process with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 In the removal of the creature, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body that can be felt, then use extraction by pinching; and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 In the extraction of worms infested in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and if the cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sunlight: if there appear any worms, then draw them out with subtle tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the cane which has this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And pour the most subtle juice into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then draw out all the wax; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop the ear with cotton as I have said about the stone; and if they do not come out strongly as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for killing worms, and you will find them discussed under distillations; and so distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this apparatus, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And if it is of silver or bronze, place it under a small hole and on top a lid to distill; and for pressing within the distillation use a well-made bronze instrument for this purpose, and if you wish take a pipette and wrap around the tip cotton suitably; then cast your oil or juice, and whatever of your medicines into the funnel, and let the funnel be in the ear; then pour into the pipette all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled out of the ear hole; and let the patient feel it within, and let the distillation be a little warmed by the fire before it is distilled in the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any opening in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by obstruction of wound, or flesh born within the ear, and these obstructions sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is lack of the opening, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Therefore, those that go deep and cannot be seen are of serious treatment in many cases, and those that one can see must be treated by placing the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent obstruction, then perform all this operation of which the form is:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind completely, so that it does not wound the ear; if the hair is of flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the hair has grown deep into the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the hair that causes the patient pain upon hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Take care to do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a cloth and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the cloth and replace it with another cloth soaked in wax that is made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling has subsided; then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding continues, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding, which are discussed in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of the skin of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This althea that comes from the eyes of birds when they are wet and dry, you must extract it with tweezers and scissors, and cut it off with a spatula of its roots; then apply powdered vitriol to the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 And if it sprouts again, then cauterize it with the subtle lenticular cautery, and after the incision, it moves better; and many times they return when some part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burnt and do not come back.
de la gresle	 of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times there come into the eyes certain things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a large gathering of moisture above and below the membrane; the work is as follows: take care if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is a slight thing to know; then make an incision wide, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with forceps, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot close it without piercing the skin a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the split is large, gather it with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment will restore it quickly and heal the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And if the boil descends inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the skin back and extend the boil with tweezers; then cut and press it from both sides; and if the skin is separated by the incision, it does not harm; and when the boil is cut, lift the eye with salt water and treat the place where the flesh heals until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is a fat that is embedded in the sheets of the eyelids above, and this happens more to children than to anyone else, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they always lie on their backs, and sleep face up, and their eyelids below their eyebrows are moist with exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the place between your fingers and feel the exinach there.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the manner of performing this is that the patient puts his head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinach from each part, then put it on him; and press between your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit as wide as the wound made for bloodletting; and cut the skin through to reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Extract it then all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out; and be careful not to approach the slit, lest you cause injury up to the eye.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the pimple does not open at the beginning of the slit, slightly widen the slit until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in vinegar and water, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the patient until he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then treat it with soothing poultices until it is cured.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When in the eyelids hairs grow that are different from their nature, and they become inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as excessive tearing and softening of the eyelids and cataracts, to the point of causing blindness; and the treatment is done in four ways: either by cautery with fire, or by applying medicine according to what was said before in the chapter on cautery, and this can also be done by incision and suturing or by means of a needle, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, then push a needle all along the thread on top; and let this be near the edge of the paper where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw the thread across the entire paper, and turn it towards the razor; then cut into the part under the paper, under the close-growing hairs, completely covering the whole spatula from the large tear duct down to the small one; then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the paper, then press on the paper a figure of an anchor, as the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you wish to raise the paper which has been divided in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Et si a tel qui a mestier (And so for one who needs) c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere (to cut a large quantity of paper) selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie (according to how the paper is softened); puis fent a tout le spatumile (then apply all the paste) sus les II lignes que tu as signiet (over the two lines that you have drawn), et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit (and begin from the large teardrop down to the small one); et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz (and let it be one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root), puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur (then place the onion in one of the two corners of the heart), puis l’escorche toute (then peel it all); puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil (then sew the two lips together with a needle and one thread of fine wool), et essue le sanc (and wipe the blood), et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans (and let the extra threads dry on the two curls with some sticky substances), se tu vues faire ce (if you want to do this); et se ce non, si n’en aies cure (and if not, then don't worry about it), puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII (then leave the stitching and threads for three or four days), puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans (then heal the wound without stitches using dry and constrictive substances); car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (because the paper heals with the closure of the wound and its adhesion, but the stitching is harmful), si com dirent li ancien (as the ancients said); et c’est ovraiges sens paor (and this procedure is without fear); et si a une autre maniere (and there is another method): et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte (which is to draw the paper in the shape of a myrtle leaf), si com nos avons conteit (as we have described), a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci (with three peeled onions according to the form shown here).
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 then cut the one that surmounts the small equal forces according to the form that is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and push it into the figure; and push another thread beside the large lip, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the leather over which you have placed the signet, as we have described; then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with wax and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the skin are turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one way or another is more skilled.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 The cure of the hairs is as follows: and it is that you turn the skin and cut inside according to what I have said, and then make two cuts with skill, and two thin threads as long as the skin and as wide as the spatula; and cut at both ends where you hold the threads; then delicately gather one and the other on what is above the skin of the eye, and tighten the two cuts strongly from the two parts; and leave it so for some days, and the skin that was tightened will die and become necrotic and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it is delayed, cut at one of the forces, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the skin is lifted, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two cuts that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 The work is such that you take a fine needle and insert a soft and fine silk thread into it. Then assemble the heads [of the needle] and tie both ends finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the shaft another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then let the patient place his head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work. Then insert the needle into all the shaft in the hair follicle close to it, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the shaft, and insert into the shaft that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out of all the shaft in the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is drawn and the hair does not come out with it, you will draw the hair to the bottom along all the thread that you have prepared, until the hair comes out of the hole above and you see it through the eye; then you will draw the hair and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh heals; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long natural hair, and raise it with that until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the infection of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or infection comes to the eye, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of the work on it is that you split open this suture, and separate its lips, and put inside linen bandages, and bind it until it heals; and it is not necessary that you use in the treatment of it things that dry out and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, then the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and wash it with water or beer and flax seeds that are cooked, and melted wax in some of the oils, and wrap a bandage around it, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your cure is that you take care it does not heal according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have said are no more than adjustments for this illness, so that it does not return according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness which is below and is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from a wound and a tear and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle with two threads on it, and pierce the flesh from the left lacrimal to the right, so that the thread comes out in two places of the flesh; then stretch the skin above all the needle, and cut with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the stone returns to how it should be, that is good; if not, then take a reamer and place it in the crack, turn the stone, and make two cracks on the side within the stone; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make an angle such that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "Y"; then remove the flesh according to the sharpness of its sides below, from what follows the stone, then join the two severed parts, and sew them with a linen thread; then proceed with the cure as we have said about softening medicines, and dressings, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And if the illness comes from a cut or stitching or cautery, then you must make a clean cut under the hairs of the skin; and according to what is said before, empty between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine with all his power how he may return the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what work and instruments are needed in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 of the suddenness of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when this adhesion happens to some men in such a way that the skin above is adhered to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and apply with tweezers, until you cut what is close to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient may not suffer that the sharp spatula does not wound the eye; and your incision, from which you peel that assembly, should be light, so that the skin returns according to its natural shape; and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is a salty water, and raise it with fresh water, and of honey; then put between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and place on the eye abundant wool moistened with egg; and after three days use honey and healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 You should know that the nail is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles a hard syphacus, and the other which is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture; when one touches it with iron to try to cut it off with pincers, no one can. And both appearances begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then opens the eyes. And lift the eyelid with your hand, then curl the nail with small pincers and extend it upwards; then take a needle and put a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair on it, and a strong thread. And fold the point of the needle a little and insert it into the center of the nail, and pierce through all of the nail, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upwards. And scrape off all the flesh of the nail that follows the prickle and the silky part to the root of the hair, then cut off the remaining portion at the root of the tear duct with all the subtle spatula and small forceps. And leave the natural skin in the tear duct so that through the incision does not come the body of tears as is customary; sometimes it happens that the nails are extended only to the onychion and to the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all with a soft spatula which has this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And see to it that the spatula does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision, cast into the eye a little of boiled silk, and made from lead, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter, this appearance of a nail is often treated with medicines; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula little bit pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 And scrape the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not thin out and the reason follows it closely, then drip from your mouth into the eye an irritant made of lead collyrium and red collyrium ground with salt, and pack the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is against you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then let it be, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of flesh in the tear duct troubles the eye greatly, then suspend it to the little finger, and cut off a part but not all, so that a body of tears does not come; then drip into the eye red collyrium made from lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 And in the eyes of some men there grows red flesh sometimes, covering the pupil and extending to the eyelids, turning them outward, and it looks like a rose on a baluster; and the work is such that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you open the eyes, and peel off all that flesh with suitable tweezers for this purpose, supporting it firmly; then cut away the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting to the roots until the end, taking care not to wound the eye during the operation; and let the incision be of spatula as we have said in the incision of the nail and small forces from which one removes the splinter, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with silk cloth or you distill red vinegar and similar corrosive medicines into it, and place a cotton pad on the eye with egg white, so that it is sure of hot abscess; and if something remains and the pus surmounts you, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that calm a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and do the same when flesh grows in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 But nevertheless, it is necessary that you treat each weak eye of the natural way; and by the accidental way, with ironwork; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear the work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If they are red veins that cover the eye, they take away from sight its function and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, first, look to see if the eye in which there is the vein is sound and has no other disease besides the vein; then treat the eye in this way: instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, then elevate those veins with all the oncine according to his skill, and let the oncine be a subtle double according to this form: xspace
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And let there be two marks by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 then carefully seek those subtle veins, and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see those strong veins retreat from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very eager in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the black bile.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you cannot find all of them in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and there is a sure sign of heat from an abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until they are healed; and this is the form of the strong:
de la fistule de l’oil	 of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 The physician so names "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is pus in it that you must incise over the abscess where it should open, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, clean it with all the instrument of which here is the form; and it is called "sharp point," and it should be made from iron or steel, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And put it on the place of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed and flesh grows, and the body of the opening is closed, and it remains so for XL days, and it does not reopen and is not pus-filled, and no bad incident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other device than to bring the fistula back through the nose in this manner: and it is that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, take a tree according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at III angles, and let the stick be thinned until the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and remove your hand from the eye by a fist, then turn all the tree until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand to his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the wound heals, the material goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 Of the eye issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is fully open without any hindrance or diminishment, you should bandage the patient; then heal it, then apply cupping glasses without pricking to draw out, then put on the eye a plaster made of vinegar and aloe and incense and myrrh, and then strain the eye, and put the plaster on with bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and fold each one four times, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount that the eye needs; then strain it tightly with a hard bandage, and reapply the cupping glasses without pricking; then remove the cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the plaster softens, you must strain it very much; then remove the plaster after one day and one night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; but if not, then reapply the plaster and the cloths and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 of the dislocation of the toe
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When dislocation occurs in the toe, it opens, and there comes out of the skin like the grain of mustard seed, and it is frightening to see; then if you see it covered, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then push another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the eyelid; and make it perforate, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cover the place of the double thread and bind one part of the toe around it, and hold it well, then pull out the needle and put on a wet linen cloth in abundance of egg; and let it be until the thread adheres with the toe, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the toe every part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eye gives a great appearance, pierce it with a subtle spatula that goes into the depth of the eye, and let out the watery moisture and let it descend from the eye, and enter quickly; then restrain it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but water that gathers in the eye, resembling descending tears, and this is not tears; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take the head between your hands from two sides, and move it so that you see the water come to the surface at your eyes; then let it be pierced, and do not let it descend, but let the light be restored, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend downwards, know that it is tears, and if the descent of the water is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If the patient sits between your hands, then take a sharp spatula and make an incision on the hardened tissue at the continuation of the conjunctiva with the hardened tissue and the cornea until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, drip hot water mixed with honey into the eye, or hot water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have here the similarities of the eye's waters in division, and what should be done to pierce them; do it according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, outside of the light from the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then take the eye's paper in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument that is called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument beside the cornea by the thickness of a ray in that brightness of the eye towards the lesser lacrimal part, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the brightness of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda path be as deep as the space from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the hardened tissue, and then place the instrument where the water is, then press it under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If he has weak vision now, then the patient sees what is before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting for a short while, and if his vision returns the second time, apply salve with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently extract Almagda by turning your hand a little; then put in some eye salve, and lift this eye back up.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then apply outside the eye gauze or cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 Now, and those who are of our time, apply a poultice with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if Almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have eyes that are too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle; then put there almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then put the tie back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the current incision, but it is necessary that you elevate the head for this reason, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If abscesses come, you should unbandage the eye before the seventh day, and apply that which soothes abscesses; and when it is pacified, unbandage the eye and place on its face a small shield to cover some days, and let it always be in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then he should leave the house gradually, and turn back to his tasks; and know that no student should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in his country they make an almagda, for which water is sucked, but I never saw any such thing in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing. ię
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 And these are the similarities of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be made of pure brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And their heads should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	 on the flesh around the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes hairs grow close together on the nose in various ways, so that some resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are those among them where there is flesh of fiery color, and there is also soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case, for the soft and not reddish hair, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, throw the wax on those hairs, and pull them out strongly; then cut with a fine sharp spatula on one side, as much as you can hold, until you know that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if any piece remains that cannot be cut, then open it all with delicate instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if the abscess surmounts you, support it as is needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood is blackened and all the pus is removed, then throw into the nose easily and with vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nose works and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not perforate as needed, know that there is pus born in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen, somewhat thick, and knotted by hand, with about one finger's width between each knot, or less; and have the patient place the end of the thread in their nostril as deeply as possible, and pull until it comes out through the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know each one in turn by feeling along the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back again on the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all the remaining flesh; and then put a lead plug in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to clean the head, on which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And it may be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and the conduit likewise; and if you wish, make a closed plug, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head; and have one handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh upon the nose
