Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 oftentimes a growth appears on the tip of the nose which is called "telul", and it grows large and unsightly; therefore, you must cut it early while it is still small, removing all of it completely, then apply cautery or hot medicine to the site; if you delay cutting until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a bluish color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess, for when it is cut, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft texture, not bluish in color, and you see that it can be completely removed, then have the patient emptied and the abscess cut without fear, and treat the site with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and severed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 know that when the solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If this happens to anyone, first consider if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a stitch, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must cauterize all the parts of their heart until they heal, then join the two lips with a stitch, and hold it, and powder on powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of stitching is such that you gather the edges together: either by needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or by thread, as I have instructed you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the lips' abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many men have hard abscesses within their lips, resembling grains of peas, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips inside out, and cut into each knot, and take it with tweezers and chop it in each part; then fill the place after incision with vitriol powder, until the wound is stained; and then apply aloes, and treat the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Many times a fleshy growth appears on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; then you must hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, allowing the sap or blood to flow; then place powdered vitriol or other restrictive and desiccating powders on the spot; and if that flesh returns after cutting, as often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: then it does not return after cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Some are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scaly patches that are ugly and rough; sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape away the teeth or scales until nothing remains; and do the same with blackness, greenness, jaundice, and other stains, until they are cleaned away; and if one removes that which is there for the first time, it is good; if not, then it begins again on the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers used to scrape between the teeth have other forms than those used to scrape off the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you cure the tooth of its pain, you delay drawing it out as much as possible, for this should not be done; for it is a very high substance until one has no reason to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw out the tooth, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient, thinking it is in a healthy tooth, and he has a good tooth drawn out; nevertheless, the pain does not leave until the evil tooth is removed, for we have already seen this happen to many knights. And when you are certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth on all sides with strong hot irons to protect the gum from every part; then move it with your fingers or fine pincers little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the tooth with the pincers. And let the patient's head rest between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 Aprés remove the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is perforated and rotten, then you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and hold it delicately with tongs so that it does not break when pulling; and you must work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take good care not to break it, and leave a part behind, and the patient will suffer greater pain than before due to the root’s malice.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act like the ignorant doctors, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth cartilage and do not bring what we have mentioned, but they often cause a great illness due to the roots that remain or the cartilage they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn out, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes out from there, which often happens, fill the place with pounded vitriol; and if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 Les formes des instruments, à quoi l'on ôte les dents en premier, doivent avoir de longues pointes et de grosses manches, afin qu'ils ne plient pas lorsque tu retireras la dent; et voici ces formes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And let them be of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling out, and let them be well-made iron, and let them have teeth to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	 from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after pulling out, it is necessary that you place cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the spot is softened, then use the pincers called "algefri", which resemble a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and that is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, then you must uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place there the instrument called "althali," which is actually pincers.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And let it be wide and strong so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments whose forms follow hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two teeth, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other irons that are in front for the reason of teeth, and with this instrument which looks like large pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And know that this instrument is such that it cannot be broken, and know that many dental instruments are; and similarly other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master subtil finds his instrument by himself according to what his work and the disease shows him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of bones, and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, he seeks the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, as is the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then restore in its place with suitable medicines. If there is decay in the bone and it is small, this instrument will extract it all:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, and the shape is ugly, and especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth grows after the tooth, and it is not in its right place, and it cannot be filed or ground; then pull it out; and if it is crooked with the tooth, then take this tool whose form is here, and it is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron, sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the claw bites little by little each day due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it is protruding such that it can be filed, then file it with a file like this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 And it is like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth bit by bit each day lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out; then flatten it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 And when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth become loose, either by impact or by falling out, and the patient cannot bite into what he is eating without them falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but to no avail; then they must be bound with a thread of gold, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then place the knot between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach wisely the other healthy tooth; then begin covering again until the starting point, and tighten your hand subtly and wisely so that they do not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then cut the heads of the wire with pincers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put them in such a way that they do not hurt the tongue; and then leave it so tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the wires break, then hold it with another wire; thus it will remain and serve throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, fresher and fresher, as we have said; and do not meddle with it unless you are wise and patient, and sometimes a form of a cow’s bone is made, and put in the place where the defect is, and hold it as we have said, and it will remain and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 Of copper to the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, one is born like that; or by accident of a healed wound; and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is due to a sudden wound, then insert the hook and cut the ligament wide; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, lift the place with rose water and alum, or cold water, then put a linen bandage under the tongue; and let the patient lick it every night, so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 Et si la perte de sang survient, applique une ampoule de vitriol sur la plaie; et si le saignement continue, cautérise avec un cautère lentigineux, qui est bon pour cela; puis soigne d'une autre manière jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et si tu vois que la plaie est de couleur sombre ou noire ou dure, au point que le patient ne sent rien, alors ne touche pas à cela, car c'est une gale; et si elle tend vers la blancheur et qu'il y a du mucus, alors applique l’onguent, et perce avec un instrument fin, et enlève d'un côté et de l'autre; et si le saignement continue pendant ton travail, alors mets une ampoule de vitriol jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit arrêtée, puis reviens à ton travail jusqu'à ce que tu aies tout retiré; puis lève la plaie avec de l'huile et du savon, et soigne d'autres manières jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes there are within the throat abscesses which are called "godath", and they are properly named the two almonds. And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the escape of blood; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or else it would burst on its own; and if it is again of pale color, and the root is delicate, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look whether the abscess is hot and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his hands be in your hands, and he opens the mouth and you take the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, whose form is this; and it should be of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 As you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the onion and insert it in the amande, and draw it strongly above as much as you can; and pull something from the cloths with it, then cut with the instrument, whose form is this, which seems like a forceps; and however the heads are curved, one against the other, and are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then use the tongs, which has this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And let it be sharp on one side and notched on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same manner, and afterwards rinse the patient’s mouth with hot water and water mixed with honey, and if bleeding occurs, rinse the patient’s mouth with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves have been boiled, and similar things, until the blood is staunched; then bandage it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman of an abscess that was formed within her throat, namely the abscess of small sense; and it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passageway was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two eyes through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened quickly and inserted a needle into one of them, then drew out forcibly and drained a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril of the nose, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the needle into those abscesses, and I drained some of it, and nothing but a little blood came out; and thus the passageway of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back, filling up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I burned it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	 of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends into the eye and it swells and lengthens, it is called «perpendicular»; and if it is below and large and round, it is called «eye».
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the pus in the abscess is subsiding, and it is thin, then you must cover it; and the one that is round and swollen but not long; and it is bloody or the color of tar or black, then you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it according to the method that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and pull it down, and cover it with one of the two instruments that I have said for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Et il est nécessaire que tu ne coupes pas plus fort que la superfluité qui dépasse la limite naturelle; car si tu coupes plus, cela nuit à la voix et au langage; et après l'incision, utilise ce que nous avons dit pour l'incision des II amandes, et soigne jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit guérie.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then it is necessary that you use anesthetic for the cauterization to reduce their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery should be very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place their head in your hand, and then press their tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and use a sharp, lively fire so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and apply the heat of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And in the head there is a hair where you put the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it harden and the stings of the medicine are soothed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the tear duct above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days it will fall off. And if you need to renew the cautery of the medicine, renew it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This cure is more effective than incision and cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and marjoram and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in a pot, and put ashes in it, and make it boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot let there be an instrument made of hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one end be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, so that the eye is damaged; after which repeat often, so that the eye dries up, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and never do this except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and place inside the head an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Often there is in the throat a bone or fish spine, or some other thing; therefore it is necessary that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the object move; and what does not open and remains in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the harsh thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of apple, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out with what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be curved at its tip so that it may enter the throat more easily, and have the head lifted up; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole or the vein come into play, nor push the bone inside; and it is better that the patient himself pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is hard; if he pushes downward, draw it out strongly with all the instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	 from the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the blood is healed as I have said in the division by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, after you have pressed the tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 Et si tu vois la sangsue, alors traie-la avec une très petite aiguille, ou des pinces fines qui conviennent à cela.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, take a horsehair and place it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the hair, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient has a fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water and open the patient's mouth, pour it in without making them choke, and move their hand frequently; and as soon as the bloodsucking creature feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument that I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot with visible charcoal, and let the lid be covered by a cloth pierced in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument; then cast your fumigation, and have the patient put the end of the reed in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that no smoke comes out, but it goes up to the phlegm; and the phlegm will now fall, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood is thus: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs to enter the throat; and it has the likeness of a bird's beak, and there should be roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many types of abscess are, according to what is remembered here after in this book, one and the other, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two manners in which one is in its very likeness, and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because the abscess of the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess of the fleshy place is different from that which comes in the joints, and each should be judged accordingly in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pricked until the boil is mature according to its nature; and there are those of such kind that one must prick when they are ripe, and do not mature according to their nature, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 Because when an abscess comes near the joints and it is left until it is purulent around, it may happen that the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When the abscess is near the main limb, and you delay perforation until it is mature, it will harm the main limb; if it is near the anus, pierce it as soon as it is ripe; and one should not perforate a suppurating abscess before the digestion is complete, except for that which is near the anus, lest it become deeper, be narrowed inside, and a fistula develop; and it may not heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And you must know the hour of perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the separation of the fever, and the diminution of the pain and redness, and the softening and ripening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must perform the perforation in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it opens up; and let the incision be long along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 En those that bend, according to this limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the opening until it is confirmed by completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before that, the body will be filled with the poison from it, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and depths of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs from it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small openings in small abscesses, and large openings in large abscesses, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where one should dig into the core, and cover; when it becomes like cloths, and is dead, then you should do as one does with blisters: and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such which one cuts like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the fingers; and there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who do not have a head, such as a soft superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and if the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw all the pus out in that hour, but draw out some of it; then pack the abscess with wool until the next day, then draw out some more; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus is drawn out; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit may sometimes jump out with the issue of the pus, which could accidentally kill the patient, and you would not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, then wipe the wound, and look to see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a plain incision, then place bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put a bandage in each one so that they meet each other; and if you have cut into the abscess and removed part of the skin, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or scraps of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, then bring cold and easy water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, then bring care and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is during winter and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then you must apply tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is during summer and the place is fleshy, then you must apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then open the abscess and dry and treat it, as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 Et ceu covient il conoistre universellement en cures des apostemes: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 de soros
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When the veins of the head cause small abscesses, and they are like those that are in tissues, similar to the pouch of a chicken, there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and like those with moisture, similar to blisters; and there are some that are hard and stone-like in nature, and there is no doubt if the blood vessels do not interfere.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you should try any instrument that is called an "entromissoire," which causes the shape to come hereafter, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Car if it contains moisture, then open it from above the long [bone].
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is removed, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, because it returns if anything is left there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will heal those who have remained at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that it does not remain at night; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess is full of fat, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and cast your onions into it, and peel it from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the cloth in which it lies; and if the surgeon does the opposite, then do as I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for a pustular abscess, in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the pustular and moist abscess, for it is lighter because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if in any of these abscesses there is no moisture at the top, and it is like the abscess that I cut at the top of an old woman; I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, it would have made a wound just like a stone. ède
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming to the head, except those which come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place for pus to exit; and treat it as needed.
des scrophules	 from scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 These abscesses often occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and there are many of them, interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is properly inside its own shell, like a nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not want to obey healthiness.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In this case, where you see a good disposition for cupping, it is similar in color to the body and moves away from every part and is not close to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you must cut above it, and scrape each part, and draw up the two lips of the vessel with a hook if you need it, as we have said in the case of head abscesses; and draw out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the needle be neither too sharp nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 Et si tu coupes la veine ou l'artère, et celle-ci ne t'arrête pas de travailler, alors mets dans la plaie du vitriol broyé, ou certaines poudres qui arrêtent le sang, et serre la plaie; et laisse-la ainsi jusqu'à ce que l'abcès soit apaisé, et que la plaie soit adoucie, et commence à pourrir.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then check with your finger if there are any small scabs remaining, and cut and clean them off.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, you should not cut this scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them now, since no excess remains due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 so it is necessary that you take care to cut the root of it, and pull strongly, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae that hold excess, pierce there where it appears dead; and pierce as the one previously mentioned, in dependence, then bring tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure with enchanting flesh ointment until it heals.
de squinance	 of a splint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 To those who have a splint, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the glands of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the illness is in the tonsil channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below III or IV circles, making a small transverse cut between II circles, or by the quantity of the syphac cut, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the throat to the entire nape, then split the heart until it reaches the kidney; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the spleen as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of phlegm from the kidney which leaps forth through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is feared, join together the two lips of the heart wound and suture it alone without glue; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is healed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to suture and cure the wound until it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the muscles of the gullet; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I revealed the wound, and found the blood that had come out of it, although it did not pierce a vein or a large artery except for the throat, and the wind was coming out strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, which later returned to normal; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "hernia of the throat," and they are large abscesses of a bluish color, and they often occur in women; and there are two kinds: natural, and accidental; in the natural kind there is no infection.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is according to two manners, one of which resembles pus in us, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it is not necessary to work on making holes except in that which is small, and test and examine all the inserted material: if you find it similar to our pus, and does not penetrate any vein, then cut it off, as one cuts a nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any; and be sure to do so quickly, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways exist in us, all of which I will describe the likenesses; and now it is necessary for me to speak about all the differences that are between our pus and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 Je dis que la sortie se produit lorsqu'il y a de la fièvre continue, jusqu'à ce que l'ébullition soit passée et que la pourriture soit accomplie; alors la fièvre et la chaleur se reposent.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 Avec le nœud, il n'y a ni chaleur, ni fièvre, ni douleur, et il contient I sifac, qui est son propre sac et selon la couleur du corps, et commence ainsi qu'une jaie, et devient gros; et ils sont selon deux semblances, soit gras, soit humide, et beaucoup de couleurs sont comme je l'ai dit dans la division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 Il convient, quand tu viens à la cure du nœud, que tu éprouves et enquêtes d'abord de tout l'instrument qui est appelé «entromissoire», selon ce que sa forme sera dans le chapitre suivant.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of our inquiry into abscesses is that you take the moistest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the heart; then according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the introducer, and beware lest it leap out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out, what color it has, pierce it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the introducer comes more moisture, know that it is fatty, then pierce it in a cross, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape each part and beware of the membrane where it lies that you remove it whole with the thread; and if you cannot remove it whole, then remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If anything remains, the pus returns many times; and if a little remains and the wound grieves the blood, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and bind the wound, and place on soothing things over a hot abscess, and continue the cure until it is healed; and if the pus is great, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and cure those who consume flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 and if the vein is throbbing against you or another, then hurry and fill the place with a broth of vitriol, and leave it lying for two days or three, until the wound putrefies, and let the blood ebullition rest; then return to the copper what remains of the thread.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the shapes of the intrusive instruments, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are also three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and they too are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, for encircling the abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles with which one sews sorceresses, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth more, and they are more proven with black lead to encircle the abscesses of fistulas; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the nails are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are nails that have two curves of three types; and there are nails that have three curves, and they are also of three types; and there are nails that have two curves, and single-curve nails, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these are sharp, and there are some that cut only from one side, with which we peel the nails so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and among these instruments are the almeds placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except on fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes we make another small instrument, resembling the peels of figs, according to this shape, with which we stop bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And it is placed sometimes in the location that heals quickly at the veins and the arteries, and sometimes according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must cauterize according to this form from line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine that heals flesh, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and continue the treatment until it is healed; and if the breast sags downwards and is softened by its size as happens to women, make two incisions above the two nipples, through two similar slits; so that one be touching the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and bring together as we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it has dissolved the rest and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard like scrofula with ribs, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
