Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment appropriate for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said for cutting scrofula, and if the wound discharges pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn together, it often leads to abscesses; the same happens with a swollen vein and abscess. And one can tell if it is due to the artery because the abscess will be long and deep; and when you touch it with your fingers, you feel constriction; and if it is due to the vein, then the reason is apparent; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the nails or in the angles or at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment of iron, and the one at the head should be avoided as well; in the case of swelling of an artery, make a cut along the skin; then work the wound with scissors, and cleanly separate the artery from the flesh until it is exposed; then insert below it an awl and have it pierce through to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then stitch up the place between the two threads with a probe until the pus comes out which is there, and let the abscess be released; then administer the treatment as for the other wounds, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of a vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand all that you can of the abscess against the entire skin, then insert the awl below the place which you are holding in your hand, and have it pierce through, and there should be a double thread so that you pull it out on the other side; then bind up the abscess as I have said, with the thread of one of two sides at the two knots of the thread; and if you fear that the thread will come loose, then insert another awl along all the thread below all the abscess to the incision of the first awl, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut away the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess of the skin and leave what is bound up; then put on a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer treatments with bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	 of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Just like abscesses come in the artery and vein, so too they come in the nerves when they are pierced, or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and hands, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the flesh, and it is in many positions without pain; and when one presses it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deeply within the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or downward or upward, and those that are in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and those that are on the head or forehead, open the skin to the air.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it by an onion skin, peel it off, then remove it and sew up the wound in a stitch, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 It happens sometimes in the belly and not elsewhere, which is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to fungi, and it has subtle roots and large heads; there are small ones and very large ones. And I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six, and the work in the incision is such that you should look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and from a delicate root; then you cut it with a wide spatula, and let there be in your presence the cautery heated.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overwhelms you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not stop tying the linen thread until you cut the artery, and let it come out without difficulty; and if the roots are large, there is fear of cutting them as well for the belly, but you can cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the vessel which is of red color and poor feeling and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Because this is an embedded carbuncle, and I will come to the treatment of carbuncles afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the abscess has become hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the abscess comes from a burn or tear of the intestines, and it is on the belly, and there are some swellings like in other injuries, or from blood leaking from veins or arteries as mentioned before, or from wind; and if it is due to injury to the intestine and its outlet, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a small thing without pain, and opens through various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with two fingers, it returns to its place, and then comes back, and perhaps it will become hard, and swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and due to strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and it appears well when you press it in your hand, and it does not constrain; and if it is due to blood, the abscess shows by these signs: large and hard, and is fixed according to a certain amount; and if it is due to gas, it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you look to see whether the appearance is of the blood from the artery, or vein, or gas.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Therefore, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is of the intestines or bladder, you must command the patient to hold his leg, and be stretched out straight; then sign around all the abscess; then command him to lie still between your hands; then go around the place you have signed with all the sponge; then extend half of the abscess above onto the large bandage; then bind it all around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the tie be loose; then work half of the abscess stretched out on the thread, and put your thumb into it, and seek the intestines; if you find them taken by the thread, release them, and push the intestines back inside the belly; and if you find the bladder, take hold of it with the bandage, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein stands in your way, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads into them, and put the two needles through what you have done in a cross that you make perforated; then press the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see pus, remove the needles, and leave the place until it putsrefies, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you can cut it when it has been softened and putrefied, then cure what is necessary, and cut open the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	 of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division the similarities of cancer, and how one should work with medicines for it, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that cancer infects the flesh, and great caution is needed in the treatment, and the ancients said that when the cancer is in a place where it can be cut off, such as cancer that is on the breast, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one must remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I have never healed anyone of it; nor has anyone ever been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile; then make him fast if he has manifest repletion; then put the patient in a good place to perform the treatment; then place your fingers on the cancer and pull from all sides, and remove it entirely without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press well the area with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding causes you difficulty with the cutting of an artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat him with other treatments until he is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: this is only «eclites»; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because it is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy called «eclites» with medicine, and the cure does not work, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as intestinal obstruction and similar things; do not touch iron there, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great strength, and he has no other disease but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed thus: lift the patient upright in your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 and at the tip, yet not so deeply that it may reach the intestines when inserted, and not injure them; then observe if the dropsy is towards the intestines: then you must make an incision above the navel III fingers straight below the navel on the left side; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the navel III fingers; and if it is due to bladder, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluidities do not run to this weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and remove it, and lift your hand all along the spatula between the skin and the fascia as if in scraping to the quantity of a nail or around it; then pierce the fascia until the spatula reaches the intended place, which is the water place, then draw out strongly, and pour this instrument whose form is thus:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a delicate silver chain, and it is of light brass or iron; and in the lower part there is one hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribe cuts the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 on the top is the ampulla, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it immediately rises onto the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at this time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will fall into a coma, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue indicate, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the cork that plugs the hole on the syphon, which I have spoken of, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating this, and extract a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to empty it but leave a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and you leave much water inside, then cure him with the burial of hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye him with wine; and cure him with desiccative medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after removing the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it should be pierced as soon as possible with a very fine needle in this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then put into the opening of the urethra a thin piece of lead, and tie it in place and hold it thus for three days or four, and when he wishes to urinate, let the weight be removed, and urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave the bladder closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose opening is small, let him be treated with a lead weight as we have said, so that it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those whose opening is not in its proper place are harmed, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies on their back, then straighten the head of the rod and the shaft in the same way as the length of a feather, so that the hole enters in the middle, as it should; and beware of blood loss which often occurs, and if it happens, staunch it with what staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these baths come to the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle lancet at the tip, and cut and clean all of them, then put on cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with refined ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is malignant, with foul color and odor, then you must bring a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it open, and if the abscess is in part on the penis, with some inside the skin and some outside, then you must first remove the abscess that is inside; and when it has healed, cure what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you cure it together, the head of the penis is not secure and may be perforated, leading to blackening and corruption in the penis and testicles; therefore, you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and beans, then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is useful in two conditions together: namely, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert into the duct of the penis a cane of lead, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair at the tip of the penis occurs in those who have not been circumcised, which happens due to wound or abscess, it is therefore necessary that you scrape it with one burning instrument until the bond is released, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is difficult to discuss this, it is necessary that you scrape some with a spatula from the tip of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate between two, and place a fine cloth of wet linen there, so that it does not harden again.
de la circoncision	 Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not the discontinuation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision at Al, and in the region, use forceps for the entire foreskin; but often the heart flees because there are two layers, and if one cuts the top layer, the bottom one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or there it receives a blow, and the pain is doubled, and in the amputation that comes from the nail, the point of the member is not secure; and in the amputation of the fingertip, perhaps the iron slips, and the work runs, and many times they are born so that they do not need amputation and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 Of the amputation that is done at the joints, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the scissors cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand and cut equally in one stroke as long as possible; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you are only doing to him what you tie a thread around the finger, and then comfort him in all ways you can; then hold him straight between your hands, and return the scissors between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the finger and blow into the heart, and draw it up as high as the head of the finger goes in; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then bind the place tightly with a double thread, then tie another ligature below the first one; and hold it for II fingers by the second ligature at the little finger and ring finger, and cut between the II ligatures, then lift the heart quickly and draw out the head of the finger; then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the cure; and put powder on it and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with a mixture of egg yolk tempered with rose water, cooked well with good fresh oil, and leave it until the next day, and continue the care from one care to another until he is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The form of strength for healing is as follows: the two heads should be even and sharp, and the heads should also be as large as the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in healing is when the heart within flees from the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your fingernail before the place makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if they pass three days, and that which is below the genitals is swollen, leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and lightly scrape off the scab; then cut as much as you can move, and be careful not to harm the part of the genitals, for it will not hurt.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Treat then the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders; and if it is cut too deeply into the heart and goes beyond, it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to the formation of a stone, or congealed blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone being in the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be placed on his knees; and his feet must be placed on his back, and he must extend his belly on the part above the back, and the patient must strain as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called a "syringe," which has this form: and let it be of fine silver, lightly made, like the feather of a bird; and let its tube be a palm and a half long, and let it be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread and tie at the end a bag of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and push it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and wash the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis up towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward into the bladder, and the patient feels it coming to the empty part, and this is not done unless according to this order because the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then draw out the thread with all the wool bag by bag, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and renew the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 of the illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When there are scabs or blood in the bladder, or an accumulation of pus, and you introduce water and medicine, do this with all the instrument called "clepsedra," and it is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and has III holes: II on one side and I on the other, as you see. The place through which the medicine passes should be such that it well stops the pipe without any addition so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when necessary; and when you wish to throw your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the liquid, and pull on the catheter inside. Thus, you will draw the liquid into the catheter, and then push the catheter strongly back in; thus, the liquid will enter and will now come to the bladder so that the patient will feel it; and this is the shape of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and beneath the breast where the neck falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you want to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the bag with that moisture over the fire; then insert the enema nozzle into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder so that all the moisture comes out evenly until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make it into a circle, and pierce it roundly all around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like an almond, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already said in the division the methods of stone extraction and medications together; and I have said the difference between stones in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stones one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that there is blood from the bladder resembling blood in its subtlety; and he urinates harens, and it weighs down on the patient's penis, and he urinates frequently, and then hesitates; and at many of these urinations there are drops; and healing is easy in children until they are four years old, and it is very serious in old people, and it is moderately severe in young people, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a clyster, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes interferes with seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move him upside down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out of the top; then have him sit between your prepared hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is fully inclined downwards; then seek and touch inside it; if you feel the stone in the opening, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall upon touching it at all, then moisten your finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and push it into its base, and look for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then guide it to the bladder's neck; then press upon your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the area where the cut will be made; then insert the catheter, which is thus formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make an incision between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the groin; and let it be straight above the stone, and your two fingers be always on the anus, and let the cut be transverse so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause the stone to come out without effort; and know that there are some stones with angles and edges: they are difficult to pass; and there are those that are below, similar to a hazelnut, and round, from which the passage is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To those that have angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, then you must extract with tweezers that are like a file at the tip, to gently pull the stone so that it does not escape; or you push underneath the instrument with a curved tip; and if you cannot manage it this way, widen the pouch at the opening; and if the flesh splits open, bind it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first push the largest to the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull strongly, and afterwards the smaller ones if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be sewn, and a larger wound must be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out constantly where the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless strive to pull it out, or break it with pliers into pieces until you pull it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon’s blood, and bandage it, and place a cloth dampened in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lay the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you dislocate it, wash very well the place with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of diafincaon and ointment of basilicaon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses or corrosions come to the wound and blood clots form in the bladder, causing urine retention that goes out with the urine: then put your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder; then wash the wound with water, ash, and salt, and help him in all ways you know until he is healed; and it must be that every time you treat him, you bind both thighs, and gather the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra, stuck inside, and urine cannot come out; then the treatment for this, as I say, is to cut open many times, and he will be cured from cutting with this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take a rod of iron according to this shape, and let there be three sharp points on one end:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the rod gently into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; then the urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken immediately, urinate on it and the patient will be healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then insert the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then urinate on it, untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	 of the woman's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It rarely happens that a woman has a stone, and if it does happen, the treatment is difficult and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well and is willing to be examined by doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is such that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled in this handiwork; and the fourth manner is such that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, for which reason it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear there. And if necessity commands this, then you must seek a midwife who knows well, and one finds her rarely, and if you do not find her, then do not seek a skilled doctor; and present to him a wise old woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command that she perform what you command for the search of the stone; and take great care if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then she constricts it under her finger, and she recommends that she insert her finger into the vulva of the sick woman, and seeks and presses her left hand strongly upon the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from joint to joint from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the penis, where it is best prepared, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the cut be small at first; then push out the reed into the wound, if you feel the stone as sharp as to make the wound larger so that the stone can come out more forcefully.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the similarities in order to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood wins over you, apply vitriol paste to the place and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stained; then return to your work, until the stone is weakened, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting stones from men to help you in your work; and if the blood wins over you, and this is due to a cut artery, apply powder to the place and bind with cloths and bandages, and do not attempt again, and leave the stone alone, and do not draw it out, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the place becomes cool, return to your work until the stone is weakened.
de hernie carnouse	 of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	  Moisture in the womb is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white sac, which is below the heart of the kidneys, containing the egg; and it is called "sac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the kidney between the white sac that we have mentioned; and these do not happen unless there is a lack.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the formation of this collection comes from weakness in the kidneys, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from striking the kidneys, and this moisture has many colors: either it is inclined towards yellow, or it is redless, or black, or white and watery, and this happens often; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is in the white sac that we have mentioned, then the abscess is round, the long sac like the shape of an egg, and the kidney does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the skin itself, then the abscess swells with some part of the egg, and because of this it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the thighs and the white flesh, one feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test the entire area with a square probe, from which the form was made before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows the probe, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to our ability and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on something a little high, and put many drapes underneath him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs at the knee of the thighs; then take the spatula lance, and cut the skin between the bone lengthwise from top to bottom until near the ankle, and let your incision be entirely straight in dividing the skin of the thighs up to the white flesh, and delicately peel it according to our ability; then pierce the white flesh full of water with a wide hole, and draw out all the water, and then put your thumbnails, and stretch the white flesh upward; and do not touch the bone of the thighs, but only the white flesh; cut all or in pieces likewise the side of him delicately, that if you do not cut wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps strongly at your work, set it back in its place when you have completed the work of the white flesh; then join the two lips of the knee of the thighs with a stitch, then cure him as the other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the egg corrupt with another illness, then it is necessary that you tie off the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the coccyx at the entire suspension, and remove the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the vein is split into two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut off the other part as you have done with the first equally, and wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and apply another linen moistened in wine and oil, and place on the two coccyxes, and place over them double-layered cloths, and tie it all up with a cord according to this method:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take II cloths, and fill them with wool scraps according to this appearance and let them be sewn together at the waist of the breeches; and one of the heads takes up the fundament as far as the back, and the other at the wrist part; and the other two heads on the two ankles, and let all the straps be tightened in the braier loop; and sometimes this string is used for cautery instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take a subtle scalpel cautery, and cut the skin of the kidneys, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac containing water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at the ankles, and peel with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cutting in all manners that you can, until you have scratched everything; and beware that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and take care of decay of blood, and wounds that come from surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether abscess or decay of blood or other things, then cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horror, then introduce perforation, as I tell you: when you are certain through the signs that we have spoken of that aquous pus is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part as wide as possible, and put the perforation through the length of the body; and let the opening be large enough so that all the water can flow out freely; then place cotton on the spot, and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining water, then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or an instrument for drawing water from hydrocephalic patients, whose form we have mentioned before; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the water will return, and it will collect again after six months or thereabouts, and when it has collected as before, then the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the cutting of this vessel there is fear in many cases, for which reason it seems to me that one should leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and similar things concerning the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 So I say that many an abscess comes to the body, and especially to the testicles; and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 That is to say, due to acid and sharp humors which spread to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; and there is no pain, but the abscess is serious; and sometimes it is an angry and hard abscess, and fiery red in color, and sometimes it comes from a knot of artery, or from swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is by the tip of an artery, it is known by the warm swelling of an abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is made swollen by a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this resemblance, and on other things; and it is that you cut the heart of the kidneys, then let the egg go up, and draw forth the white from the yolk, and deliver the chalazae from all around the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already hardened with these things born, then it is necessary that you draw out the yolk and cut it; and if it is airy in the white, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that thinness, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is in the posterior place, then you must cut all of it, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until he is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bud, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient becomes very ill when he goes; and the treatment for this disease is almost as dangerous as the one before, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary for you to make the patient sit on a high seat, then place the sling of the testicles down to your thighs, to all the vessels that are close to the vein, and hold them tightly, and stretch them greatly; then cut with a sharp spatula wide along the transverse towards the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and tie again to the other end; then cut them straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt moisture; then treat the wound like others where one may insert a bone, so that no vessel bleeds where it nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels have veins, it is necessary to draw the testicles from all the vessels; so that the bird does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot help.
de la routure dou syfac	 From the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The happening of this rupture is by the section that comes to the shoulder, or the extension on the belly in the region of the hips, for which the intestines descend from this rupture into one of the testicles; and this rupture is either in the shoulder or from the extension of it, and these two types occur very often due to many causes: by striking, or jumping, or laughing, or lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the sign that it is from the extension of the shoulder is that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is equal towards the depth, because the shoulder presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is when it is of the section of the hypochondrium, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin near, and this is for the exit of the intestine and the body from lack of the hypochondrium.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the intestines descend with the intestine and are held back, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these treatments with iron due to fear, for which it is necessary to avoid them.
