Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of the work is such that you instruct the patient to reintroduce the intestine into his hand within the wound if he can reach it; then let him be placed on his back between your hands, and lift his thighs; then pull the peritoneum upwards, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert the leaves of the tail into the incision according to what you need to open the wound, and make it such that the egg can pass through; then scrape off the peritoneum that is under the skin of the testicles, so that the white peritoneum is exposed from all sides; then insert your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white peritoneum that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second peritoneum, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second peritoneum; and then move to the right hand within the peritoneum of the testicles, and raise the white peritoneum upwards to your left hand, and lift the egg with all the peritoneum towards the tail; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and release that which is held behind the binding; and feel with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white peritoneum, and if you find anything, push it down into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the rear part of the peritoneum that is after the skin of the testicles; after the tail, then cut the heads that appear from the threads, so that there are 4 threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the peritoneum that we have said is under the skin of the testicles with a strong thread of 2 parts; then wrap the heads of the threads, and bind them strongly with 2 parts, so that none of the servants who nurse it can enter within, where no aposteme may come; and put back the thread as we have said before, long 2 fingers from that one; and after these 2 threads leave the peritoneum that is under the peritoneum of the testicles the width of a finger; and after everything else according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles, so that the fluid flows, and heals, as we have said before; then apply moist wool in oil to the wounds, and put the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes the white flesh is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling off, then it should be rinsed with hot water, and apply what we have said above, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this manner, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as the manner of tying a ligature together with a needle, so that you tie the vessel after cutting lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessel falls off; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 When there is an ulcer in the anus, as we have said, it opens up; and do not let any of the intestines fall into the testicles, and if they do fall, that is bad, and it returns every hour; and yet if it stays too long in this state, the wound or abscess grows until the intestine falls out; and this happens due to the expansion of the abscess which is in the anus, as we have said, because it is expanded, then the place becomes soft and swollen and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and that is for the patient to lie on their back between your hands, then cut the inflamed place of the ulcer wide according to the width of three fingers; and then draw out the abscess which is under the skin like a thread, then take the thread and put it on the visible part of the abscess; and press deeply into the stomach, then sew the two visible parts of the abscess onto the head of the thread, and sew one and the other; then draw out the head of the thread, and do not cut or extend the thread or anything else, as I have shown you in the cure of the tear in the intestines; then cure it like a wound.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The syphilitic person is confined, and there is no appearance of scabs, and the cautery is moved to this place, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Often the skin of the testicles is softened in certain men because the parts inside are made soft and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that one make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and if you wish, first sew the excess of the softened skin with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as the other wounds until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
dou chastrement	 Of the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; it is only necessary in two ways: the first is that the physician knows how to respond when asked and knows the treatment; the second is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to aid us, such as goats, sheep, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say then that castration is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one we do by attraction, let us sit the beast in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them with your hand, as long as they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Du chastrement de taille: it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspending rope, and strike each testicle once, when you have well skinned them; and leave some of the subtle sperm that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is better than that done by attraction, because in attraction there may remain by chance some parts of the testicles, which causes the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	 Of hermaphrodites:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism occurs in men in two ways: one is that between the two testicles there appears like the nature of a woman's genitals, where it has hair, and sometimes urine comes out from there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it extends from the wrist like a rod and two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is to cut off all the flesh together, and treat it as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine flows through the skin of their testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	 Of the swelling
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Swelling is a gathered flesh on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must press the excess of the swelling into your hand or a cloth, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that blood does not flow out, then treat it like other wounds until it heals; and another flesh that grows at the mouth of the womb, and fill it, and perhaps it will overflow, and it is shaped like a cow's udder, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it becomes necessary for you to cut it, as we have said about the tendon, then continue the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	 of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic is when the woman's nature is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has occurred; or it is caused by a harmful substance, whether subtle or thick, and it is formed in the womb, or on the sides, or underneath, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and knowledge of this condition comes from observing the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling appears near, seek for yourself two or three [remedies].
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, and the procedure is as follows: place your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread; then extend the two lips very well, so that the subtle suture is round and there is an overlap of the stitching; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and have the woman lie down every day, so that it may not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the suture is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the stitching is of flesh, suspend it to an onion and cut it; and have hemostatic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, with plenty of egg; then prepare a wide plaster of lead, so that the wound may not heal; and let it be this way for a long time, and apply a dry linen bandage; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in the flesh comes a tumor, it should be cut according to this manner, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an infected abscess that is in the flesh, one should not attempt to cut.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which usually protrude, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thin; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and thinning, when they are deeply embedded in the flesh and do not appear to touch, then the cure is not by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the edge of death, which one can sense, are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 It is necessary therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then apply the tentacle with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicines to stop bleeding, such as oak galls, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she bleeds continuously, then have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if he faints, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, have him apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without cutting; then take wool, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of hawthorn with old wine, and have him apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess has settled, treat the place with onion until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and looks like a sharp thorn, then you should cover it as I have said before; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 of the abscesses of the buttocks
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscesses come in the buttocks, such as chancres and pious abscesses and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other illnesses that I have spoken of in the section on classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess that comes on the breast, which is not among the abscesses that swell up; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see whether the abscess is acute at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the abscess mature until the pain is relieved; then have the patient sit on a seat, and he should have two small seats on which he leans, and place behind his back and gather his feet towards the side of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good ligature; then give him a drink towards the left side, and bring to that place the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the breast, from which later comes the pus; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument there, that you first drive in the reed so as to know the depth of the breast, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the breast with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he place the cone of the instrument on top, and that he wets the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens and one makes an incision with the hand softly, then it must be covered at the top with a poultice of lettuce; and when the cavity is emptied, then you must place on the wound tents moistened in rose oil or in dry green oil; and put the tent outside the wound at the bottom of the linen cloth, and put above the linen cloth and over the bandage clean linen moistened in water where malves are cooked; then cure after two days of anointing according to this, until it is healed; and sometimes one raises the linen cloth and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then of water with lily roots and long aristolochia cooked; then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is festering in the flesh, then you must be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is first necessary for the midwife to recognize the natural shape of childbirth, and its sign is when you see a woman pressing downward and desiring to smell the air: then you should know that the child wants to come out; then know that this birth is according to the natural shape, and the issue is under the head, and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, you must press lightly on her belly so that the child comes out quickly, for when it descends upon its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the mother is purified of her superfluidities by good cleansing; and those who come otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 And it sometimes happens to the feet, and it comes strongly to the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes onto the belly, or the back, and by chance it turns onto the neck, and other evil shapes; therefore, it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and skilled in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes out of the head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth violently, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, where the women hold her; and let her strength arise from oil or cooked fenugreek, and then the nurse puts the little spatula between her teeth, of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cut the caul, and scrape the nail until the moisture within flows out; and press the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman must be given an enema of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will issue.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands issue strongly, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet high; then tilt the stool onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during this; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that was previously mentioned, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's issue on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes onto its feet, it should be pushed upward; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then take hold of one foot and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When he jumps to his hips, command her to take hold of him, and make him sneeze by condition; if he jumps further, then let God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he does not jump further as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 For then he goes easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come further as we have said, then take musk from the testicles and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and apply on the woman's genitals inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to the ribs; and when she is well soaked, give her a drink of honey, and place it under her tongue, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 Of the child's birth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, let the midwife place her hands little by little; then let it be raised onto its back, and let the feet hang down, and let it lie on the bed; and bend its hands little by little, and then take the hands up towards the belly, and remove the cushions from below, until she is ready to deliver. And if the child does not come out, then take hold of its feet and move them strongly, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands inside; and pull the child little by little; and instruct the woman to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 Of the child's birth who comes sideways with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to devise a way to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, then make the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, then lay her on the bed and spread her legs widely; then bring the muslin that I have described; and if she does not deliver, then make her sit on the chair, then study to return the hand; and observe the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and instruct her to take as long as the child issues forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 from the child issuing on its neck, with hands spread and face turned towards the mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and observe carefully; and when it is equal, place on top the natural muslin with height and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and instruct her to take; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 of this same manner to all the second
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out this way to all the second, strike the second with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child presses on its face and neck, then cut from the mouth so that it is not retained, and let the child die; then push the child back in as much as you need to put it, and instruct the woman to take some time: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange and do not live, unless rarely; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the membrane which divides them, which is attached to the mouth; and sometimes they come out naturally as one, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out severely, then treat as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and do it quickly and lightly, as she does; and act so that he may move to safety.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or many up to fifteen, and all are fully formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the bandage knows all this, for perhaps similar things happen; so act according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	 of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are compelled to work by hand; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound health, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman must be raised on her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her legs lifted up; and let the midwife take a thread from two parts, where she may bind the woman to the bed so that she may not be moved at the child's descent; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with muslin cloths of althea and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint the midwife’s hands with these oils and these cloths; then insert them lightly into the womb; then seek one place where she may insert the hooks so that they are suitable for it, and take care if the child is ready to descend on his head; then place the hooks in his eyes or neck or mouth or soft palate or under the beard or in the pharynx or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then insert them into the finger and middle of the ribs; and it is necessary that she holds the hook with her right hand, and places the tip between her left thumb and forefinger, and inserts all her hand lightly, and places the hook in any of these places that we have said, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 and then drive one against the other or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then keep them equally in motion from side to side, so that it may come out, and let the points be toothy to hold it, as shown here in the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 and if a piece remains, then apply some oil from the wound with your fingers to that part and draw out the other part; and if nothing remains, place this point in a higher spot and do this until all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and it cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it up in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut it off at the joint of the foot or ankle, and so you should do with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment at the mouth of the womb is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if he is stuck in the belly or breast, then you must pull him out wrapped in a cloth on your hand; and open the belly or the breast, so that the moisture inside is corrected; and if the other members are removed and the head remains, then push your hand deep into the womb, and draw it to the mouth of the womb; then put one or two ounces, and pull strongly; and if the mouth of the womb is narrow due to a hot abscess that has come there, do not work hard at it, but apply moist and greasy things; and administer plasters, and sieve in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on its side, and you can put it flat, then do as we have said for the living child; and if one cannot, then draw out the bowel piece by piece, leaving nothing of the intestines behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, treat the abscesses that come to the skin as we have said for other abscesses; and if there is discharge of blood, apply a restrictive bandage, and provide other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had died, then another was born on top of it, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time, an abscess came to her womb, and it swelled so much that it burst, and she began to have great stench.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to the care, and there I thought for a long time, but the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I placed a strong attracting plaster on it, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was greatly amazed by this, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 Then I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I washed the wound and drew many bones from it until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time thus, always exuding a little pus from the place; and I did not forget this chapter except that when the master finds something strange, he should know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 To return the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, by which we turn the leaves; and at two turns of the two keys of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 However, the horns of the restricter should be more delicate and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wooden piece should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the leaves one finger, and in length a palm and a half; and between the two levers there should be two adjacent pieces of this same wood, which are firmly fixed in both ends, half a palm long or a little more; and these two pieces are pushed into the mouth of the dislocation to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more delicate and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling tongs; it should have at the two ends two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; when you want to open the uterus with the whole instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet dangling and her legs spread, then insert the two adjustments into the uterus together, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the uterus, until the vagina does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument is all covered and their appearances are multiplied; and when the surgeon has prepared them, then the work is swifter, and higher for men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not destroy the instrument before you have prepared it, because its needs are not negligible.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcibly, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she expires by this means, so be it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, then take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over the fire; then place a reed through the hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapor enters the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 Si il saute rapidement la deuxième fois.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and is not strong, then instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or althea musk, and then insert it into the vulva, and seek the placenta; and when she has found it, take hold of it and draw it gently straight, so that the membranes do not tear during extraction; but it must be moved slightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the membranes is tightly closed, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and the fumigation of herbs; and if it does not work with all that we have said, then take care not to pull too hard during extraction; but it is necessary for the one who is at the mouth of the membranes to tie it to the thigh of the woman, then administer an enema of tetrapharmacum oil; and it will rot and putrefy, and come out strong; however, when it rots, it causes a foul odor in the stomach and head, and injures the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 Si it is then necessary for fumigations that are suitable for this: some of the ancients have proven fumigations with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retaining the flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it is made of glass like a tube, and one places the thin end in the vagina, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be over the charcoal, and continue until it is completely consumed, and then another one should be started.
de percier lou fondement	 To pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born whose anus is not pierced, but rather closed by a thin membrane: it is then necessary for the midwife that she pierces this membrane with her finger, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and takes care that she does not touch the membrane; then she places a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then an ointment cure until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not heal properly, place a lead plug in the hole, and leave it for several days, and have it removed when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this plugging occurs suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that sudden opening: and if treated as we have said with the lead plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	 of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come below the anus are nodular, and those that come near the anus or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and also moistens with white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by the fact that something comes out or passes when the patient defecates, and sometimes even a bone.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 And so it is with fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and they reach as far as the hip joint, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one can know the penetrating fistula in the anus, and the non-penetrating: it is that you insert your finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if it has twistiness, then insert a thin tent of lead, or a horse hair, until you feel the tent or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of pus, wind, or faeces as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; and hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 And when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the passage of the urine, then the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, then the tendon comes to that place; if there is no twisting and the pain is evenly distributed around it, then it always bulges out, and neither medicine nor ointment for healing is of any use; and in these piercing fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and foolish doctors waste their time trying to treat them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In one that is not piercing and is not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have proven, and it should be that the patient lies on his back between your hands; and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then you insert a tendon of iron, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tendon comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger, if you then feel that the tent has been perceived; and if it is discovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then know that it is persistent; so do not bother with it, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Nevertheless, it is said that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the help one does, is to heat a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and insert it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times, so that you know that those burnt hairs are burned, which are like a bird's feather; and then cure the moist tents with butter, until that hair comes out, then cure the injury with healing ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent is not pierced to the bone at the base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula where this covering ends; cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward constantly, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be freed and will fall off; then clean those faulty flesh parts that resemble a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the blood flows, and passes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Car the fire cautery brings together two good things: that is to say, the burning of these hairs close by, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of wet tents with butter or crushed herbs, until the place throws off the wetness, and thus the burned hair falls into the place; then treat the wound with hardening ointments made from tough flesh, and these are the dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 Car when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if the fistula reaches completely to the anus and is separated from the body, then push your finger into the anus and seek for it there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between the two there is the vein or sinew or hair, if it is about to break through, there is no cure except by the means of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way down, or if you can, put a tent in and treat as before; but do not go too far so that you do not cut the support which holds the anus, and cause excrement to pass there without control; then treat, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either by tent or by another suitable instrument; then cleanse that faulty hair in the wound as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside of the anus: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this way: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is in the side of the foundation near the skin above, so take a tent pierced at the head in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And put a twisted thread in it, and push the tent along with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is persistent in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that hole, as you push your finger into the foundation; and pull out the head of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold them to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and restrain it sometimes, until the threads cut these tissues that are between the two, and break; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 If the fistula does not break through, have it pierced in every way that you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because it is not appropriate to cover the wound for the binding if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The tip of the spindle-shaped spatula used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting, and not on the other, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	 hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there may be a few or many of them, and blood flows from them frequently, and there may be one or several, and they are outside the anus and at the edge of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes flow a little citrine water or a little blood, and have the color of flesh. The treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to wash himself in order to go to the latrines, until the anus comes out strongly, and the hairs appear; then hasten, and grab it with tongs or hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots. And if the nails cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth or cotton, or a piece of flannel; and pull them with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle on some hot powders that are suitable for cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat with other treatments until healed. And if the anus cannot come out, then enema the patient with a biting and harsh enema to wash what is in the anus, so that it can come out freely; when the patient squats, and the hairs are strong, then the treatment is light; and it is that you grasp them with your nail or tongs, and cut them, then treat as we have said, until healed, and let him fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 Of dryness of the intestines or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Many times there is dryness in the intestines due to natural constraint and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you must scrape off the skin with a lancet or your nail, so that it does not moisten; then cure it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it bleeds greatly and is raw; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	 Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formica is a small hairy creature that goes very deep into the body; and sometimes the cold finds it, and it is felt just like death by trembling, and it comes over the whole body, more in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is such that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong bull feather and place this cane on the tremor until the circle surrounds the tremor completely; then turn your hand along with the entire cane so that it goes all around the tremor, and place it deep in, and extract the tremor by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see it this way, then do so with a cane of brass or iron in this form, and let it be sharp below and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 Nor should it be perceived, in order to move towards the two, and move closer And if you see this way, then cauterize the tremor as it is shown in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or gold, or of melted brass or iron; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those [instruments] that are prepared for the treatment of children who are weak and in pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The shape of the small and large enema is thus wide at the top, where the stomach is tied like this:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there should be an opening where the stomach is tied, as you see, and the end should be perforated inside; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole. And let the stomach where the medicines are placed be made from a beast’s bladder or parchment, and it should be perforated all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one finger's breadth of space. Then put a strong thread through these holes in the shape of an X or twisted together, and assemble the stomach like this:  [insert image of a goat here]. And when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then enema; and that is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar substance, then insert it gently; then the minister should squeeze with both hands together until it is all empty, then remove the enema, and make the patient lift his legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold it as much as possible; and if he sleeps through the night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you enema him in illness of a prolapsed belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids or abscesses in the anus, let the enema be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of a thin enema by which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the strike of a stone, or cut by sword and knife, or spear, or club, or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members. And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 Je dis que quand une simple plaie vient sur la tête, et les os ne sont pas brisés, alors tu dois voir si c'est à cause d'une chute de pierre ou de choses semblables, et la peau est tout de même déchirée et la plaie est grande, et tu crains qu'un abcès chaud ne se forme : alors fais immédiatement saigner le patient de la céphalique elle-même si un peu de sang sort de la plaie, et que la saignée soit du côté opposé à la partie blessée ; et que le patient évite l'excès de vin et d'aliments grossiers.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.
