Et s'il ne veut pas saigner, alors il doit réduire sa nourriture, et ne boire ni vin, ni manger de viande; et place sur la plaie, si un abcès chaud y apparaît, du coton imbibé d'huile rose ou de vin stiptique seulement; et s'il n'y a pas d'abcès chaud, alors mets sur la plaie, si elle est fraîche avec tout son sang, et qu'elle ne soit pas déplacée par l'air, une poudre que je mentionnerai un peu plus tard; et si le vent l'a déplacée, alors place quelques onguents, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 Et si la plaie est grande comme celle d'une tailleuse d'épée et semblable, et les lèvres ne peuvent pas se réunir par tentes, alors réunissez-les par couture, comme je le dirai pour les plaies du ventre, de la couture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 And if the wound is exposed to the bone, and deep, and only held by a small piece of flesh, then shave it off; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as heads and cooked grain, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find that the skin has rotted and it reaches to the bone, then cut off all the rot, and throw it away, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with cortices, and it cannot be stanched by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and it is that you put in this powder which closes before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and make it into fine powder, and fill the wound, and bind it strongly, so that it heals well and joins with all its flesh; and then bandage it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this only with quicklime, when one has neither frankincense nor dragon's blood, but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the burn has moved the wound, even in summer, one must not put this powder on it; but rather some digestive ointments, or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey, until it discharges pus; then proceed with other cures until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, draw it out with fine tweezers; and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 from the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head; but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other device than to leave the treatment alone and not to put anything restricting on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, as hot water in soft water, mixed with rose oil, and also wash it with hot water, and other stones of smaller size according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is deep and swollen and full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut and blood comes out, cauterize it, and sew it up, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat or the heart is cut, and the passage is preserved so that food can pass, sew the heart on the back of the throat, but do not touch the throat, but put it back according to its natural shape; and then bind it gently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has affected the bone, pierce it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound becomes gangrenous, and the issue is dried up and made smooth; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if there are bubbles coming out of the wound as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder in it at the first hour, nor bind it so that it does not burst deeply, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put on an astringent ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; thus there will be no spasm, no evil heart tremor, nor breathing difficulty; and when you see the bones healing well, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure it then with dressings and other treatments, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and work, always know that there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, either in the worst or back part, then treat it like those in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is close to the bone, and has hit pieces of it, then seek the wound, and remove the splinters if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound fester, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 Of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes jumps out some intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, for which their introduction occurs; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one puts back less easily the intestines in, if one does not put them in hot; because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, and enters less easily, and therefore the medium wound is better, because one brings back more easily the intestine to its place than with the others. And know that the suture of the belly is according to IV manners: the II common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the body are II other sutures proper to the other wounds; nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and something of the intestines has come out, it is a difficult thing to reset, which can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a small cloth in hot water only, or cook in hot wine and cinnamon and cloves, and rinse the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes this wine has a restraining effect, and it is better than all for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine in water in which althea and mallows have been cooked, for by this it is easier to insert a little; and if it cannot enter, then widen the wound with an instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, for no one should cut unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: cut inside in the curve and not outside, and here is the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is opened and the intestines leap out, then reset them carefully according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, then you must make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the belly, then put the head and the feet higher than the lower parts, and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then focus your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must proceed as I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what you have prepared, then take into your hands a pious minister who can hold all the edges with his hand, and gather the lips; this is the common way of sewing, and it is that you take one needle or more according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' width from the head of the wound, and there insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is under the skin within, until you make it pierce through that part, and gather the two heads of the siphac together in four; then pull a double thread around the needle on two sides, then gather the two lips of the wound properly, and then leave two fingers' width, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need for the needles, until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and thick, because subtle needles cut all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: therefore, they should be medium-sized; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and damage the wound before the sewing; then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not wound the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths on the heads of the needles to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this way of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because a needle can be substituted in the second sewing, which is common, and it is that you gather the two lips of the skin and the two lips of the siphac together with one needle where there is a medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, then remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner in which clothes are sewn; and put the width of a small finger between each sewing; this sewing is known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines protruded well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 Je remis son intestin après qu'il avait été en dehors pendant vingt-quatre heures, puis je pansai la plaie jusqu'au quinzième jour, et ensuite je soignai la plaie, et il fut guéri.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I put cotton on the wound twice a day, and I washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced through the center straight on, leave the head of the thread where you passed the needle, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside; and the intention of this suture is that you sew just like the furriers make the furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side and take it back on the other, until the suturing is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of suturing, which Galen properly calls, is such that some perform it by naturally joining the two parts together, and they apply one end of the thread to the other end in this manner: insert a needle into the near end of the thread, and make it pierce only that place, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part until inside, at the two ends of the thread; then make it pierce both from the outside part until inside, in two other places of the thread that are on either side; and this is the common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said these words, and some attest to it: one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the injury is in the middle of the belly, the suturing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then set it to burn again the intestine, and the skin; then put on powdered meat; and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound boils; and stitch the thread, and let the sutures and mirach be sewn; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to exude pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many conditions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will infect the main members, then it is necessary that you soak a light linen cloth in tempered oil or rose oil and place it around the joints and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in his bowels, which often happens, then give him an enema of tempered red wine, and similarly if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the thinness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the intestine comes out of the wound, put it back as is, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black or dark, then you must tie off the black part so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut the part between the ligatures, and hang the two ends down from the lower part of the wound until they protrude to ease the extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is cut and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into an abscess, from which excrement and gas came out; I treated it as best I could, and did not stop treating until he was healthy, and the place healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw him stitched, I feared that the patient had an ailment in his belly; but there was no ailment, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large-headed stitches, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the stitch has opened its mouth, place it over the two lips so that it closes its mouth; and then strike its head, and this holds so that it cannot untie itself, then place another stitch afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 That chief so fastens in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that it be very thin, and then tie at the head of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and return it to its place; and this method of suturing for wounds is nothing more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal veins, there is no remedy or healing, except for skillfulness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 Of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it has healed, is universally called "fistula," and also when it has burst and flows with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And the fistula according to truth is called "nodation" hard and white, in which there is no pain, and it is also open like a bird's feather; sometimes it flows clear pus, and at other times thick; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that has not healed and has no flesh, it is not cured except for one of the IX causes: namely, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or the place is rotten and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or because in that region digestion is slow, and healing is late, and by nature it is swollen; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or it is necessary that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is made by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the sinuses, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and some that occur in the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula which does not come as far as the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you wish to know it, then take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, probe it; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it with a subtle probe of boxwood, for boxwood bends easily around the curvature; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot probe it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will pass from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then probe it wisely as best you can, so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve there, and cut deeply into it, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the foulness and corrupt matter that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in the right place, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then insert moistened probes in healing medicine, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine may corrode the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply dressings with clean flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If the vein or nerve is injured in a principal member, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, then scrape it so that all the corruption is removed, then cure with things containing fat until it heals; and if it does not heal, and it goes bad again like before, know that you have not reached the bottom: reveal and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it heals in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with tongs, then pull it with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them all, do not leave any one; and if moisture hinders you and there is no mistake or fear, then cut and moisten and cover with flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place on the wound a substance that promotes putrefaction, and let it be until the place is rotten around the bones; then the bones will be more easily extracted. If it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then wait only until the corruption has removed all the blackness, then dress the wound; and if there is a great part of putrefaction, reaching to the marrow of the bone; then you must cleanse and cut away all the way to the putrefaction, and then treat it until it is healed. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 It was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that entered the body, so much so that matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, for which there was no cause to open it; but the physicians, in their foolishness, worked on it until the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out of it, and it became a fistula, and through it came many holes that all exuded pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians tried to cure it for about two years, and there was no sage among them in the art of healing, until I was called upon it, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the holes with great force; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je planted a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one met the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Je therefore hurried, and cut into one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it to be corrupted and rotten, and the corruption reached inside the bone; I removed what appeared to me of the corrupt bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for what I removed; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it did not heal; and then I tried again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I strove to heal the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and drew it out completely, then treated it with medicines; and it healed and joined together quickly, and there was no need to redo the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Car for the evacuation of blood he often fainted, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, which had a good disposition and caused no harm or opposition at all, neither when leaving nor when arriving.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sewn together in this manner: take a thread and tie it to the end of the bone that is open; command someone to pull it upwards; and put another thicker linen thread above the first thread, and tie it onto the flesh on top of the bone, and stretch the end so that you can draw the rotten flesh out from below, and reveal the flesh on the spot where you want to sew, so that the suture does not hurt the flesh; and place a splint or a board under the bone to help remove the rotten flesh; and it must be sewn until one can see and feel the corruption, and then sewn again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place a coal underneath, and then pass silk from one side to the other through the corruption, and let the silk be as long as the corruption is deep, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and pass the silk through the bone where it contains, from the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the wrist of the foot, that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must seek out this corruption, how it opens for you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let neither the vein nor the nerve be contrary to you; and know that the incisors and silks for cutting these bones are many, according to the placement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their fineness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare a tool for each similar work; and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so consider the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	 from fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head is consumed either from within or without; and when you have treated this ulcer with the cure of medicines, and they are not beneficial, it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the place where the ulcer comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the loss of the limb; and the sign is that the limb turns black, as if it were burnt by fire, and then putrefies after the blackness, then this corruption spreads from one member to another, and affects the whole body; therefore hasten to amputate, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous beast, such as a scorpion or viper, and the ulcer is at the tip of the finger, then cut it off, and do not give it space to spread up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes up to the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, that is death, and there is no other remedy except in the quantity of its virtue; and do the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is such that you bind it above and below, and stretch a assistant down one of the bindings, and another assistant up the other binding, and you remove the flesh that is between the two bindings to a width of one finger, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or saw, and put on each side a strip of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient with another lesion and abscess there.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, cauterize the area immediately or apply some restricting powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in his foot: there was a darkness that resembled a burn, and this corruption first came into his toe of the foot, so much so that it spread throughout the entire foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and he was healed; and a long time after, the corruption returned to the toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I placed reactive things on him after cleansing the body, and the corrosion could not stop; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I hoped to expel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, because the man's vitality was weak; and he became completely desperate and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and he was healed; and I have not heard of this happening to anyone else for any reason.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy place and stays there so long that it creates a large collection of pus; then it roars and bursts, and the pus jumps out, leaving the spot empty, like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as delicate cloth, but does not reach the bone or nerve. Such an illness is called "sinus," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cut all around it, even when it is thin, like cloth; and does not close due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with a clyster in this manner: look to see if the breast is large, and the excrement coming out of it is of foul odor, then use a clyster made from Egyptian medicine, which is made like this: take equal parts of asafoetida, oil, and lead oxide, put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and administer it as a clyster to the breast, and constrict the opening; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; sometimes you should use a clyster of ash water when this medicine is not present, and it should be that you take vine wood ashes and pour water over them, then strain them, and administer as a clyster until you know the breast is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then use a clyster of water and honey in which there is a little lead oxide powder; or you can use a clyster made of honey and mixed wine, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the skin soften; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then use a clyster made from what produces flesh in it, which is that you take diafinit plaster, mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can use a clyster of some medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned in the treatise on ointments; and if the breast’s opening is small and the clyster tube cannot enter, then widen it slightly with an iron rod, and insert a tampon of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, sew it up and leave only one place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening from which the excrement comes out is on top, then cut it open in a lower place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Car when the abscess is fully formed, it does not allow flesh to enter; and if you cannot cover the chest as you wish, prepare in such a manner that the abscess runs to the lowest place there is, for when the abscess is full, it does not allow flesh to enter. And if you cannot cover the chest as you wish, prepare in this manner: that the abscess runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the abscess; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut strongly around the opening of the chest a little wider than the first, then extend soft ointment over another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the opening of the wound to lighten the abscess, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the opening of the chest, often remove to remove the abscess, and know what comes out of the abscess, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that comes up on the opening of the wound, know that the chest is already healed, and health approaches; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the chest throws out undigested matter after many days, know that the chest is not well-aired.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison comes out after a long time, do not despair of your health, for the health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are men in whom putrefaction of flesh occurs slowly in their wounds, and others who experience the opposite; and if undigested matter comes out of the chest after many days, know that the chest is not well-aired; and if the chest is slow to air and is distant, then bring together dry and moist substances but use them as dry medicines, such as ointment diaphonitus, for it has a great amount of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment diaphonitus, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equal in substance; then let it steep and use it; and the same thing cooked thickened makes better, when ointment diaphonitus is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them onto honey when it is on the fire; and then glue a cloth, and place it on the chest; and sometimes we administer long aristolochia, and celestial lily roots, which are like vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them, and make powder, and put onto the honey that I have mentioned, and use; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has gone deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on ligaments; so heal according to the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A paronychia is an abscess that occurs under the nail of a finger or toe, and sometimes it can occur in other places; and when it becomes old and is not treated, a pus-filled abscess forms, spreading and throwing out pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly all the way to the end; and there is corrosion down to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the tip of the finger or toe is swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail with an iron instrument, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is of great help if the bone is healthy and the fingernail is intact; and if the nail presses into the flesh, begins to prick and wound it, then you must place a thin wire under the nail that touches the flesh, lift it up, and carefully and lightly cut off that flesh. Then apply healing medicines on the remaining flesh until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger begin to rot, cut it off at the first joint, as mentioned before, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is struck, and swollen, and there is great pain, then it is necessary that you cauterize it first. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by slicing diagonally across it, and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something soothing on top.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two bones that grow in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is one with bone, and sometimes there is a claw; and sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, where the growth appears on some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 That which grows on any knuckle of the finger does not move, and that which grows at the joint of the finger by chance moves; the size of the fleshy one is light, in such a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 That which grows at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so hold onto the chisel.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes primer la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The sudden meeting of the two [bones] occurs at birth, or from a wound, or from burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Therefore, you must cut this joining so that the bones can return to their natural shapes; then place between two bandages or cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not join again; or insert two fine lead plates, until the site is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly it happens to one of his fingers with the palm, then strike that knot as is necessary.
des vils	 Of the filth
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large and swollen, full of black bile superfluities that affect many members of the body; and it occurs more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 It is therefore necessary that you administer some purging of bile to him, and then heal him with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is according to two methods: the first is that one strikes it, and draws out the black blood; and the second method is that you lift the vein, and draw it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The cutting is done in this manner: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large vein is made subtle. Then hold the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or in two or three, with a wide cut; then draw out and pull strongly the black blood towards your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength can bear; and then bind it, and instruct him to eat dark-colored foods. And repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The raising of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then place it in a basin and bathe the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no basin, heat it by the fire, and then cut towards the vein from the thigh to the knee, or in the part below at the ankle; then remove the skin with a razor, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when felt; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white rope. Then push the razor down until it is raised from the skin, and then lightly cut another place in three places; then remove the skin over the vein until it appears, then raise it with the razor as you have done, and cut another place as you have done before; then cut another cut, or several if you need them, then raise it, and cut towards the foot, then draw and raise to the second cut. Then draw from cut to cut until it all comes out strongly, then cut; and if you cannot draw and raise it, insert a needle with a very strong double thread all the way in; and bind and draw it, and push downwards, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and take care that it does not cut, because if it cuts, it cannot be drawn or raised, which is harmful to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, place moistened wool in wine and rose oil on the wound's site.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not chop it; and draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron with which one cuts the face is curved, and does not cut, lest it should cut the vein; and it has a large curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein. But let it be thick as we have said, and here is the figure:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is found in the legs, in dry places where no grass or tree grows, and on land that has no moisture; and perhaps it can appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the putrefaction that comes under the skin, just as snakes and worms are found between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of linen from one and a half to two and a half palms long, along with the knot, and leave the linen hanging on the leg. And every time it protrudes even slightly, wrap it again with the linen and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, but do not cut it at its base until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will re-enter into the flesh, and cause an abscess and gangrene in that place, and a serious illness. Therefore, this vein should be treated little by little until the end, so that nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when treated for five palms long or ten, came out of one man up to me, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, a stream of blood or pus comes out, and pierce through to the bottom so that everything comes out. And clean out the matter that is inside, and apply medicines daily on the spot that prevent gangrene, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there is less blood, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and much pus comes out from it; so it becomes less blood; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
