Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "beef disease", because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body, up and down, and one feels its presence when it moves from limb to limb, until it ruptures the skin where it passes, and exits; and it is infected with the rotting of some humors, like worms and serpents and leeches and ascarids in the belly; and one fears its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot do so except when it is moving: therefore, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong band tightly, then cut on top and pull strongly; and if the pus is in deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire on top, until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it will affect the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, then press strongly below under it, then cut on top, and pull strongly; and it is necessary for the patient to use purging of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors, and to abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it move like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, just as if quicksilver were running from one place to another; the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while later it ran all over the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it always went around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 Je me merveille beaucoup comment elle se déplace ainsi d'un membre à l'autre, car je n'ai jamais vu cette maladie de cette façon auparavant.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 However, I had seen many who had felt pain move from one place to another, but I had not seen it as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and open veins, and for this reason appeared those forced winds; and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this disease being treated and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then apply [remedies] on top and below hastily, and then cut until that constrained wind is expelled; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it with those that expel winds, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of their types is such that there are those with large points and small ones, and hooked ones, and welded ones; and there are some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some with parts; and the arrow that strikes a member does so in two ways: into a principal member it enters, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes one of these members and the signs of death that I will tell you about later appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many cases; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the signs of the head when an arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and if the membrane that is on the brain swells, there will be blindness and dizziness and confusion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixing of the senses, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there will be discharge from the nose or the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and from the wound white moist matter like pus, and also as a stream of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, hold back from treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a finger, and black blood flows from the wound, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of an arrow that never leaves a foamy spittle from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And if the arrow falls into the cover of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and causes great pain and great sorrow; and all the members from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance some undigested flesh may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and a little feces come out through the anus, there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and urine spurts out and flows away, and the patient feels great pain; know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and pelvis and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to me once that an arrow fell into my forehead at the root of the nose; I pulled it out, and drew it from another side under the skin of the ear, and was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And a man shot an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was bent, and he could not reach it except for the tip towards the wood, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without feathers; the man was healthy, and no evil happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And he shot an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers; I shaved the beard, and acted so skillfully that I removed it, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And he shot an arrow at a man, which had fallen into his stomach, and I thought that he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut upon the arrow, and engineered it, and drew it out strongly, and he had no evil incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man into whom an arrow fell in the back, and the wound was sealed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition at all, nor did it find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And you see another man, into whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sealed over; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and very many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And drew an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose, and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the arrow was completely sheathed. I was called to the care after it fell for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I perceived it all as a subtle tent and did not feel it; and he felt stinging pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I placed on the spot a plaster that was both attractive and digestive, so that the place would not swell; and the spot where the arrow entered appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the plaster for fewer days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so. 》
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed on the wound a corrosive medicine for fewer days, until it was open, and I explored it, and felt the head of the arrow that was anchored in place; then I applied to the opening of the wound this same corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and after three months had passed, the wound healed so well that I applied tongs to it, but they would not grip; then I did not cease to subtilize and devise ways to handle tools, until one day I took hold of it with well-made tongs, as will be described at the end of this chapter, such that I drew it out, and closed up the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you may apply your care to those which I do not mention, for the book cannot contain everything; but the wise master finds a new work and a new instrument, in descending from strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit from the members into which they are struck except in two ways: either through the place where they entered or through another part; and those that come out through the place where they entered are arrows entering fleshy places, and this sometimes happens now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not come out now, let it be until the flesh is rotten around it, and the opening is wide; and likewise if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce all around with a fine needle until the place is widened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the incidents that I have mentioned happen to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it until it becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow comes to the suture, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach as far as the marrow, and the patient remains for some days without any bad incident, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is stuck in this way and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is hidden within the body so that one cannot see it, then search the entire body; and if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then widen the wound until it is large enough; and if you can, pull out the arrow, and if the arrow has barbs by which it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck to both ends as much as you can, and then bend or break the barbs of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, for you would extract it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the place around is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is against you, then apply what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve or vein, and devise a way to safely draw out the arrow quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient as he was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help there can be. And if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another part, or if it has made an opening in the body, or if the skin is swollen in that place so that one sees or feels it clearly: cut then above until the tweezers can grasp it, and then pull it out; it must be done now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out stronger; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push all the way to the shaft; and if the shaft has broken off, and you see that a pushing instrument is being used, then use an instrument with a cavity, so that the point of the arrow enters into the cavity of the instrument; and then push hard, and if the arrow is broken off, then insert the instrument with its point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls into the chest or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close, and you can cut above, if you cut; and take care not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows is like a bird’s beak, and see here its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to insert into the tip of an arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The shape of the pincers for inserting and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are XXXI veins from which one can bleed, sixteen of which are in the head: two veins after the ears called "herbech"; and two arteries in the temples; and two veins in the eyelids called "aspires"; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the tip of the nose; and the two jugulars in the neck; and the two veins in the lips above the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins commonly used for healing are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, located on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; another is called "fast," composed of the cephalic and basilic, which the common people call "vein of the heart"; the basilic is on the right side, which the common people call "vein of the belly," and it is above the fascia, being the one used for healing, clearly visible at the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the savatelle is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, which has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the left wrist, and the second is the saphenous at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse," which is at the other ankle; and in the other leg there are also three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of wounds after the ears helps with old catarrhs and headaches; and the quality of the bleeder, as I tell you, is that you take the patient's head and rub the place where the wounds are with a rough cloth; then let the patient strangle their neck with a rope until two wounds appear behind the ears in two hanging places from the head: find them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, signify there; then take the lancet, and push it under the wound up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way along the wound, and cut well the skin and the wound two fingers' width across, and make the blood come out as much as you want; then hold and bind until it is healed; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, this is worth for an old migraine, and a headache, and a habitual cataract, and against tears of agues in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeder is as I say: and it is that the patient should stretch his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and he feels the pulse under your finger, then indicate with your finger; then lift the skin over the vein high to your fingertip, and push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and cut it as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it; and then bind it well, and leave it until it heals.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Li sainie de la voine dou front
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Et la targe de la teste sus lequel li sancs issist sanz douleur; puis en li metras une bandelete, si com nos avons dit, et couvrira la plaie par dessus.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 Et se tu vues que li sancs n’iue tant que tu voel, delie le malaide, car trop grant sainee fait la teste enfler.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in two arms helps with the eyes, and with the tinea, and with the redness, and with the pustule in the eye, and with the diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting some cord, as before; then bleed, and let the blood flow across, a little long from the flame, a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 And if the flame is delicate, it might break; then make blood flow as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding of the vein in the nose is effective against fever, and madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is such that the patient strains his neck, then holds his nose with your left hand, takes a delicate long flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it for one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The bleeding of the two veins helps in the constriction of the artery, and at the beginning of infection, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and in inflammation; and the quality of the bloodletting is such that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein from the arm widely for a short time, then draw the temperate blood, as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and constrict both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 de la saignée des veines
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bloodletting of the veins of the lips above helps to cool the mouth, and to heal gum infections, and lip cracks, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the quality of bloodletting is to make the patient sit before you and grasp his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are recognized by their blackness and because around them there are small black veins: cut both, and if you do not recognize them or are in doubt, cut the largest of each part, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The bleeding from wounds that are under the tongue aids after bleeding from the carotid artery, and this is for constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeder are such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks under each side a black vein: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The wounds of the needle with which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either by pricking with all one flame, wide and broad, or with a fine olive-shaped one like cutting needles, and it is called "hare's nail"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the wounds.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The form of the merlin flame is very renowned, and it is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary for opening the veins filled with gross and apparent blood, which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more subtle in its aim, and it is for healing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in diseases under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach; and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery and blood begins to flow, it must be stanched, as I have said; and the flame should not be pointed, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and replace it with another one; or you seek some of its remnants, or you close the vein in its place within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a knife-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to know the place of the bleeding, then first you must extract the arm so that you can touch the place until you recognize the pulse; then mark the place with a sign, and then tie off the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-like flame; and be careful not to strike an artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et si tu vois saillir en haut ainsi comme l'urine d'un enfant, et le sang est rouge et subtil, sache que c'est le sang de l'artère: hâte-toi donc, et mets ton doigt dessus longuement, puis ôte ton doigt si le sang s'arrête, ce qui arrive souvent; si lie le bras, et laisse ainsi, et que le malade ne le bouge pas; et qu'il ait peur, et qu'il ne le bouge pas tant qu'il soit guéri.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	 If the blood is not staunched and it prevails, and a physician is not present to you, then cut the artery if it is open, because the head of the vein retreats; and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a piece of fig bark and split it, and take one half and bind well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that's good; if not, then cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding is not harmful in many conditions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein in the middle is such that it draws blood from above and below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful for the nerve below, and if he goes too deep, and finds the nerve, and it swells, and the wound is harmful, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often protrudes, and if it does not protrude in some people due to its subtlety, then you must cure it with the anesthetic instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, incise it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The veins of the cephalic and saphenous are beneficial, as they draw blood from the head and help the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in the flare of the olive or at the flare of the myrtle, for this is the safest of all veins, because under it there is neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 However, one should seek the lightest place, and it is not serious if one misses the first time, and starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some men when one misses the first time, but it is not serious.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is not induced except to maintain health and to prevent future illnesses. The bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are available: namely, cephalic, fast, and basilica. It should be bled at the beginning of spring in youth, and in autumn and winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; it should be bled on the first or third day, two or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The bleeding for illnesses has no set time, but rather when necessary, by day or night, at any hour and in all seasons; and it is not right to bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a pregnant woman except after the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 The old who have passed LX years should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when someone wants to be treated in any way, it is necessary that he cleanses the intestines with a light enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the superfluous rottenness harming the main members; nor should one be treated who is too full of food or drunk to the point of being intoxicated or dropsical. And if one wants to be treated after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, travail, waking, and fasting, and those things that totally weaken the vitality, whether by the action of the weapon or of the body; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drinks and medicines if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtilize the blood, and treat the vein of the foot around the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day against work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the practitioner's hand be higher than that of him who is being treated, and rub the arm two or three times, then pull the vein slightly, for when it is too narrow or shallow, the blood cannot flow; and then he rubs the place with his hands until the veins swell and are felt; then the practitioner moistens the flame with a little old oil, then places his right hand over that vein under the place where he wants to treat, so that the vein does not burn and fail at the strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Because there are veins that flee like ropes of a rope maker, and so there are those that are full of ventosity, such that when one applies the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if he works the vein, the wound is too narrow. Therefore, the rope maker must be skilled in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 And if the vein is worked the first time, it is good; if not, then one must try again a little below that place or quickly above, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the place is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for a day or two and do not bind the arm: perhaps such abscesses will come; do not enter the bath, then resume the vein opening if he wishes; and if the passage is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that as much blood will not come out as you would like, then thrust all of the flame straight into that passage itself; and work a little hastily, before the place swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bloodletting again, and apply some oil to the wound, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place is the oil better than the oil; and thus administer the oil in each bloodletting that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing makes a poultice and compress of them, when it is placed on the wound; so it refines the blood and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess occurs, which happens often, especially when it is not bled strongly except at that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and apply to the place a sponge moistened in water and in salt a little hot, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the place after some days any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm; and if you see, apply some aloe or myrrh mixed in juice of calamint, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And many times an abscess and appearance occur at the site of the tonsils: place then your hand there, and if you find the spot soft to the touch of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid then putting anything on it of what we have said, for perhaps the blood is coming from an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the spot, and then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw on each according to the amount of its virtue, and according to the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 For if the blood is black, let it issue until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it out until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And he who is strong and healthy, if he needs bloodletting, one should make a wider wound for him, and the flame should be wide; and for the weak, do the opposite, and one must bleed little by little and often, and one should bleed by cutting across, not by pressing; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and nerve damage, and it is better than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for him whose body is lacking in bloodletting, one should give moistened bread in apple juice; if he is heated, then draw blood three or four times, and if he has a cold complexion, let him chew before the bleeding moistened bread in musky syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints from blood loss after a great deal of blood has been let out, then it is necessary that he drink broth made of meat and subtle, fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have mentioned in the section on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to bleed from the arm and bleed again another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great blood loss, that he be bled little by little according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if one wants to bleed from the arm after the first bloodletting and he has a strong body, then let him be bled seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after nine o'clock.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And who wishes to heal from another place, must heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 Because there is much blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, a large quantity must be drawn out, and the hole widened until it bleeds freely; then when you have considered all the conditions of healing, place your hand on top of his thumb while he heals, so that death does not come in place of the blood; and this happens often when the physician is negligent; and when you see the arm release, and make the blood come out a second time, and the hole closes, do not press too hard; nor if it curves, let him extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds a second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, so that the frozen blood at the mouth of the vein comes out stronger, and place a little cloth soaked in water on top, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not compress it until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if there is a need to bleed a second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The vein in the arm is healed in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the method of healing is such that the patient places his hand in hot water until the blood vessels are red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then heal immediately across, not wide or long; and the opening should be large, and heal very close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not flow out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the healing from this vein is safer than any other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, and boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, and se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; and n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, and puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, and n’en puet issir.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn blood as much as needed, place oil and salt on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The bleeding from his left hand is as valuable as the illness of the mouse, and does everything similarly to what I have told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The bleeding from the saphena is as valuable as all the illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the stomach, and retention of urine, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient should put their foot in hot water, and rub over the vein until it bursts, and bind on the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many rains; bleed then in the widest vein or at the ankle, for that is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And if you cauterize on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and cauterize across like when slicing; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and allow the wound to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the cauterizer fails the first time, then begin again a second time above a little bit, for the place is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the ankle of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic wound is at the ankle on the outside, and its cauterization is worth the pain of the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the nature of its bleeding is such that the patient enters the bath, and winds four times around the ankle, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then bleed in all ways that you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cup it, for the place is hollow, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you cannot find it, then bleed some other vein that opens on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; make the blood flow as much as you wish, and then loosen the bandage, and place cotton and bind it tightly; she is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	 of cupping bleeds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Ventouses are made from horns, or brass, or glass; and ventousation is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this ventousation which is without pricking is done in two ways: either with all fire or without fire; and the ventosation which is done by pricking and blood extraction is done in fourteen places on the body, one of which is entirely on the top of the head; another is in the middle of the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and the ventouse under the chin; and the ventouse on both shoulders; and the ventouse on the buttocks; and the ventouses in both arms; and the ventouses in both legs; and the ventouses in both ankles; and this ventosation does not draw blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person at all, as one would do by bleeding a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness one must bleed, or for custom, we administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, and in the middle, and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see nothing but blood and wounded and dead things and similar.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially when it is mid-month, we order them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding of the nose can help with the coldness of the head … that affects the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuating the entire body; and this ventilation is in place of the cephalic bleeding, and it should not be used by those who are of a cold complexion or have catarrh, because it does great harm to them; and for that reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold head conditions.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who bleed often become stupid, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower out of fear of becoming stupid.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The cupping on the neck is in place of the bleeding of the head and basilic vein, and therefore it is valuable for constricting the bladder, and for the cleavage of the urethra, and for dropsy, and for repletion; and one should not insert too much, because if it adheres too firmly, it causes stupidity in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 When performing ventosations at the second rib of the neck, it is effective for headaches, migraines, and strangulation, and for toothache pain, and it is in place of bloodletting from the basilica; and you must instruct the patient not to press too hard with their hand, so as not to cut an artery, and prevent excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 Ventosation under the chin is effective for mouth diseases, and for gum infection, and similar diseases in the mouth; and it takes the place of bloodletting from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 Ventosation on the shoulders is effective for illnesses caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Ventosation on the ribs is as effective as bloodletting from the three main veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to probe too deeply, because the area is bare of flesh, and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping glass that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases below, and it must be large, and made of brass, because it needs to draw well; and if by chance it was delicate, it would break; and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from the whole body, and they are good for old pains of the kidneys, and of the bladder, and of the spleen, and they remove fever; and they are placed on the two sophenes, and the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause lethargy in many constitutions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The way to apply the cupping glass is that you should first place it empty, and suck quickly, and put it on hastily, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; then strike, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are such people who have dark flesh, and clear pores: thus, it is necessary to strike only once, and make large wounds, and one deep cut; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to subtilize the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw little by little from the blood, we must suffice with only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want to take much blood, then we bleed frequently; and if the blood is thick, we strike deep, and the end result should be that the heart is pierced suddenly, and those who have thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, must anoint the places of the cups with pungent and dissolving oil: in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and in winter, with cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is large and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whom we heal has tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar waters.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And the one who has much moisture should be treated with easel, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have large superfluities should be treated with old wine, or water of suet, or decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things; and one must not heal with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and he should not sleep after ventosation, and he should wash when he is to be ventosed and when he has been ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And watch if he who is healing is irritable, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; then it is necessary that he take cold things, such as grape pomes and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eat poultry, and meat of castrated animals, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.
