And if such abscesses come about, do not hold it firmly until the seventh day, and place a damp cloth with oil rose on top; until such an abscess is appeased; then hold it, and the manner of holding is that you place the poultice on the fracture, then bring the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and wrap the bandage, and hold above the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is immobile, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint than the others on the fracture; let there be two finger widths between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to extend three fingers' width beyond the break on either side. Then draw the splints together as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, stronger and less spaced apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the splints' placement and tightening, as we have said, at the time when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt that the abscess is hot, then leave it to be bandaged until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the bandage every three days for any itching or swelling in the area, lest the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you receive it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such incident occurs, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and every hour of the day or night watch that the shape of the broken member does not move, or that the ligament is not weakened; then receive it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first subtle; and when he begins to improve, let it be thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days altogether; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and onion-based remedies to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, it takes one day or two months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm break
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two scapulas", one of which is small and follows the elbow; and the other is large and is located below the little finger; by chance, only the large scapula breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small scapula is broken, the restoration is easy and the healing swift; but when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small scapula that is broken, then it should be stretched slightly and made straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large scissors, he must be held more tightly; and stretch him out on the pillow, and dip the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the pillow in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then let the servant stretch his arm to the part below his hand, or to the thigh, and another servant to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the physician will set him straight, according to his best ability.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if there is a break with pieces, place each one in its proper place; and if any of them sticks out and touches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, cut above and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; take care accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the treatment there are abscesses like this, then attach a piece of cerate made from rose oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth lightly on top until these abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the cerate, and apply the plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint for the break be always a little thicker and a bit wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints on the arm in several positions: either if the break is in one bone or two; and tighten more at the break than elsewhere, and always less when moving apart, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths over the break be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is tied, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And wrap the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must wash the limb with hot water until the itching is appeased; and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the binding, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, treat it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you notice that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it with a poultice and leave it like this for some days, until the nourishment reaches it, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things we have said happens to the patient, then do not unbind them for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or if it happens around [the neck], then let him hold his hands to his neck, and let the collarbones be equal, and he should avoid movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps even in twenty days, according to the composition and complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that on the back of the hand and between the fingers there are few breaks, and only swelling occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or swollen, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on the stretched cloth, and let the minister stretch the broken bones, and let the healer align them well, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and compresses, if there are abscesses, then place a bandage according to the size of the area; and let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 Et si le brassière est autour du ventre en dessous de la plante, faites une bande de tissu, et dites au patient de la serrer autour de sa jambe cassée ; puis serrez avec un long morceau de tissu, et que l'écharpe soit aussi large que la paume de la main, et serrez-la comme il faut.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the fracture is in the finger, you must place a bandage on top and another underneath the limb, so that the hand remains open and straight; then bind the whole hand, and secure the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the fracture occurs in one of our fingers, if it is a dislocation, set it straight as needed; and bind with the limb, and if you see this, place a small straight bandage to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or any others, set it straight, and bind with the healthy finger that follows; or bind all together in one binding, which works best, or place a bandage on top, like for the thumb; and take care in restoring and positioning the abscess properly, and support whoever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is clearly seen when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one ligament is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches his ligament equally to his part; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligaments be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be by the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone equally with his two hands, as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, unless pus comes out. xspace
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down before returning to your work and your treatment; the healing will be done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap a double-layered bandage around the break II or III times, leaving the ends sticking out, then turn the leg so that the heel comes up to the base of the big toe, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee underneath, and the ends of the thread should come up top; then wrap the bandage around the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the break, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to even out the pressure, then begin to tie III or IV times around the break; and as you go higher up the break, press less; then hold the II ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and bind III splints that are on top, then return underneath to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and press it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as there is no abscess or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, dislocate it, and address what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then one must remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then one must split the place, and pull hard; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Sometimes the hip is broken in such a way that splints are placed there, as in the shoulder and the arm; nevertheless, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the hip is restored within 40 days or a little less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the calf of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and this happens with any wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is done by placing that which is broken equally on both sides, as close together as possible; then apply a plaster, and if needed, place a round bandage, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the precautions we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses and similar conditions; for each incident, use what is appropriate until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones; one is called by its right name «mustelz», and the other is called «foscile»; and every fracture occurs as it does in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns to the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several fragments, let the traction be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have completed your work, take two bands of wood that encircle the leg from one side to the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap around it twice a bandage above and below, and bind it in the middle as well, so that at this point the leg cannot incline to the right or to the left, and thus it is good. Some add a shin guard of the length of the leg, made of wood, to prevent movement, and one does this properly for a fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg to see if there is an abscess or other accident, and heal it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot break and the two feet, and only fragments are found in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is a breakage in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground as if he wants to walk, and now put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and dressings above, and place a small board with two full heads below the foot, then bind the foot firmly, after which you wrap bandages around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 Et lorsque trois jours ou quatre seront passés, alors délie le ligament, car tu trouveras les os égaux, qu'ils soient cassés ou disloqués.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if any of the toes are broken, then restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot that table which I have mentioned, and bind it firmly. And if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it stand on top of the board just below the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And it is necessary that you not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have spoken of them; and treat each incident as it should be done.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the vulva is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her towards the back part, and hold her from behind; then fill the vagina with cotton, putting in as much as I have said; then make the woman stand up, and lift the buttocks little by little, and then the cotton jumps until it comes to the entrance of the vagina, and the bone returns with the stick; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: thus the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and attach a reed to its opening, and blow up the entire bladder inside; then inflate the reed strongly, so that the bladder is swollen inside: thus the fracture of the vulva will be healed; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the fist of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said in the hipbone; and these breaks are not hidden from those who apply themselves to study and use, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the break indicates in many ways the right path for restoration; consider it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose’s throat and put the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it there for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 with break and wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or the shoulder bone or similar, that he be cauterized now, so that the cauteries we have spoken of testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then close it with vitriol, if you do not have anything else, then begin again to restore the breakage in that same hour, or that day, if abscesses like these do not come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if abscesses like these come there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause evil to happen there.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding from the flesh exposed, then it is necessary that you place it lightly with your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extension is not ready for you to set it even with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument that has VII or VIII fingers in length, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and therefore the physician needs III or IIII, depending on what he needs for each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the end, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," which is why the curved head should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push once until it returns, and let both be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the end of the bone until the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument for this, either a knife or scissors, to your ability; then scrape off what remains in the bone by sharpness and small flakes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is not in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound any ointment or other thing that contains oil, lest it bring forth putrefaction and corruption; then apply splints after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times the foolish physicians have done this, and have brought death or corruption upon the patient; and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that a bad accident might happen, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not put on scales; but wrap around, instead of scales, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two enlarging the wound in the place, then remove everything you have put on at once, and apply a healing salve to the wounds, such as tetrapharmakon salve and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And you should unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And the limb should be prepared in such a way that the wound drains easily downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but rather breaks open again, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all the loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an abscess or other form of corruption occurs there, you must cure it according to what is said in the previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for many times death follows, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 of the wounds that come upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see it after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is unsightly to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Therefore take heed if the node is fresh: then administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, and resin, mastic, and similar others; whether you take one of these things or all together, and boil them with stiptic wine or plenty of egg or honey; and put it on the node in cloths, and bind it well, and do not untie it for many days; and then loosen it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you can bind it on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is such that it removes all inflammations from the limbs; and if the node has already hardened like stone, and needs to be removed, cut it open, and make the superfluity appear; or have it cut by some surgeon, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 Of the limb which is weak after the cure
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the bone fracture is healed and afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bandaged too tightly and not as needed; or because there were too many bandages, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to very large movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is to make the patient eat and make the body soft until his blood increases in him; and administer baths to him and give him joy and happiness; then apply poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment to it, and frequently wash it with warm water until the nourishment reaches the limb; and may it return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 of a twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are exposed, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: therefore, do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb all over again; and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great evils come from them, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and the torture are recent, it is necessary to soften them with hot water, or boil herbs that soften, such as leaves of mallow, roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diaquilon, and take the juice of mallow, and mix it with grease of goose or oil of sesame, and apply the plaster on top; or take fat figs, and crush them with hemp seed, and similar medicines that weaken the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes dislocation is removed by continuously and extensively rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And the member should be gently moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the twist is revealed and hardened, like stone, and needs to be removed with an iron tool, it must be cut down to the bone, gently with a sharp scalpel; and care and skill should be applied to the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint is displaced from its place, so it cannot move, and the limb is deformed, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation happens to someone, they must immediately be brought back to their senses.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car if one waits too long, the place swells up, and even if one resets it to its place with great difficulty; therefore, it is not necessary that one moves it when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient bleed, then leave him until the abscess subsides; then wash the member with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as it comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It often happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are a little removed from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the chest, and the saliva runs out of the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns through many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and whole, then you must quickly reset it, without delay; and in such a way that the attendant holds the patient's head, and the healer places his finger in one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are free, to balance; and instruct the patient to relax their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the healer balances it until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the resetting is difficult, even if it is both jaws together, then soak them in hot water and oil until they can be easily reset; do not delay the resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is well closed without softening, place on moistened cloths in a poultice made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head should be between two pillows so that it does not move to the right or left, nor should they make an effort to chew, but take light food until the pains are removed, and the jaws are bound; and then he may masticate what he wishes lightly, and he should not work to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set correctly within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and sudden faintness follow, and perhaps diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, know that it is fatal; and many times he who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the jaw
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The jaw cannot dislocate from the inside or from the end of it, and sometimes it is dislocated downwards, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on his back, and extend his arms; and then press firmly on the spot with your palm, and it will return; then apply a poultice and bind it, and hold it in place; and the head which is towards the side cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply a poultice and bind it, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus also is the shoulder head brought back when it has left its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates to the lower part of the shoulder blade; and the second is to the upper part of the arm; and occasionally dislocates to the upper part, which happens rarely; and does not dislocate to the rear for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and often dislocates downwards towards the shoulder blade, especially in those who have little flesh, for it easily jumps there; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men through a blow or break, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary that you test it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it descends towards the scapula, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and below the scapula at the backbone the top of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and so, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly at the backbone; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the assistant lifts the patient's hand up, then places their fingers underneath, and lifts the joint with force upward to its place; and the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it underneath; thus it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and let the assistant prepare a softening and soothing mixture, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and administer it; then let the patient be placed on their back, and place under the arm a pad of wool, neither too soft nor too hard, then let the physician place his heel on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pull the patient's hand; and another assistant holds the patient's head so that it does not move downward; at this point the shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it thus, reset it according to this manner: and it is that you have present a man who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight beside the patient's side, and place his shoulder under the patient's arm, and lift the arm upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant pulls the patient's hand downward toward the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, then put with him something heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And one can also reset it in another way: and this is how you drive a long stick into the ground, so that the head is as round as a fist; it should not be too thick or too narrow. Then place the patient on top of it, but let there be soft cloths underneath, and the patient should be lying along the length of the stick; then extend his arm downward from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick two arms' length long and four fingers wide, which has a head round enough to enter deeply under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then lay the patient on top of the draped log so that the log does not harm the patient, then place it under the patient's bottom; and extend his arm along the log, and tie the shoulder to the log, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on the step of a wide ladder, and let the hand hang down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is inside, in whatever manner, you must place under the bottom a round piece of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with flour from the mill, with incense and egg white, over all the shoulder and around it, then tie it firmly under the bottom, and twist the ligature over the plaster, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain so.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he eat little, so that the limb may be comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then let him eat more after V days or VII, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is moved out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three cauteries to it, as it is said in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after VII days, and the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	 De la dislocation du coude
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick member with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And it is necessary that you reset it before an abscess forms there, for if an abscess were to form there, the resetting would be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the resetting is thus, when it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arm be spread out, and the hands of the patient according to the member around, above and below, and push the joint back together at its roots or in the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strike with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong traction; and if two people are ministering, they should extend the arm, and hold it with two people so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side, after you have wrapped a double-long and wide cloth around it; and when the shoulder reaches the joint, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint strongly until it returns; and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg yolk, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is firmly in place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then recommence the bandage and the ligature, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly placed; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels stiffness after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then wash and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or place on the joint a piece of fat sheepskin, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then place the sheepskin back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see, place a moist, warm cow dung with butter on it, and bind it up; thus it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is light, more than other joints However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the very hour that it is dislocated, lest the place become swollen or hot abscess comes.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the returning is done thus: you put the sick hand on a table, and the assistant extends his hand, and the doctor places it evenly so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns However, you must look to see if it is well in place; then let the patient lay the back of his hand on the table for extension and returning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician should place their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is good. If not, then constrain it with soothing poultices for abscesses like this, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after some days, then the joint remains crooked; and it does no harm to the patient except that while the hand is moist, it cannot grip anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is no other treatment except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the poultice we have mentioned, then restrain it and leave for V days, then release it and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, soak it in hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated at every part, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then stretch out the finger and push the dislocation towards your thumbs until it returns, then support the head of the finger and turn it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for II days, then make it equal that day; and bind it as we have said, and unbind it after a day, and make it move, and rebind it again; and do this often, until it is healed, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the shoulder blade or neck is dislocated, and there are multiple dislocations, then there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign of this is that the ejection comes out without will, and he cannot hold it back, and often some member becomes softened, whether the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the shoulder blade moves in four parts; that which moves to the rear is called "gibbosity": the cure for this is that you return if the gibbosity is from childhood: then there is no cure nor healing of all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients describe ways of healing with great words, where there is not much benefit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; and in the same way that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot cure except that which comes specifically to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched on his back in an equal place, and have support beneath him so that he does not get hurt; then stick a log at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie one rope under the saddle of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two helpers should know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two logs; and let them be well tied, the logs as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine firmly until it comes back.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three spans in length, and place it underneath the patient, and let the patient lie on their side, and strike the head of the board underneath the patient, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do the same for the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you plant two stakes at the head of the patient, one span in length, and near the feet two others, and let there be between each stake, above and below, a hand's width in length; and let each stake have a hole, where the shoulder fits, and let the stakes be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes, let there be a turning stake, around which the ropes turn, and let there be two small stakes near the turning ones, one hand's width in length, to turn the shoulder; and then tie the rope that is among the pulleys to the shoulder towards the head, and the other rope to the other shoulder towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his own stake all the way along the rope, and the master straightens the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equal, then put on a drying plaster with plenty of egg, and then the bandages, and then the bandage of a tablet three fingers long, which should soak the place of the jaundice and the healthy part of the spine, then bind with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing, then you must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have mentioned before; sometimes a piece of lead is applied, and sometimes it appears in the rear spine of the back, and one might think this is a dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, which is why there should be no presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the hip and shoulder joints, dislocations occur alone, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and it is more often dislocated on one side than the other, and rarely in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the sign of its dislocation inside is that when the leg of the patient is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee to the fire; and the place which is near the swollen abscess is hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.  |  And the sign of its dislocation inside is that when the leg of the patient is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee to the fire; and the place which is near the swollen abscess is hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of those to whom it happens as a result is that this event is contrary to the previous ones.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the sign of those to whom it happens beforehand is that they will support their leg well according to its condition; nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make them walk, they cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and the ankle swells, and when they go, they step on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of those to whom it happens afterwards is that they cannot extend their knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place below the hips.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The return of this type of dislocation is such that you should consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, there is no cure for it; and it is not necessary that one has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.
